Unemployment Relief Bill Rejected

(London) The Conservative Party proposed an amendment to the unemployment relief bill last night, proposing that child allowance should be at least three shillings. The government expressed sympathy for this amendment, but believed it was not feasible because the relief funds available to the entire family of the unemployed would be reduced as a result. Fifty members of the Conservative Party supported this amendment, and another hundred members did not vote. This amendment was finally rejected by 177 votes to 125 votes. The government only gained a majority of 52 votes, which is the first time in the history of this parliament. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

France Will Prohibit Gold Exports 46

To Be Implemented After Budget Balance

(Paris) Former Minister of Commerce Leinard stated in the Privy Council today that the value of the franc is likely to continue to fall. He said that the depreciation of the franc is inevitable unless the cost of industrial products is reduced or the French budget is balanced. Otherwise, there is no other way, because the current absorption of huge amounts of gold by the United States has the greatest impact on the value of the franc. The current Minister of Finance Martin said that the government will never reduce the value of the franc, nor will it abandon the gold standard. French bankers unanimously stated that France has a large amount of cash reserves, with 74,882,707,000 francs. Although it has been repeatedly exported abroad recently, it still has no impact on the value of the franc. It is expected that after the budget is balanced, France will immediately prohibit the outflow of cash abroad. The reasons for the recent instability of the franc are: first, due to the absorption of cash by the United States; second, due to the impact of the Daladier political storm; and third, since Germany withdrew from the League of Nations and the Disarmament Conference, the French people have been worried about Germany attacking France. Furthermore, the recent stability of the currencies of the Netherlands and Switzerland and the continuous inflow of French gold into the Netherlands and Switzerland are also major reasons for the instability of the franc. (National News Agency dispatch on the 20th)

(Minli) Today, Minister of Finance Maddan announced the French government's financial policy in the House of Representatives, saying that in short, this policy is to adjust domestic and foreign prices, rather than engage in the manipulation of the national currency. The high domestic prices are due to the protection of French agriculture and the result of the war. The government should adopt the least painful method to restore the country's greatest activity, but merely reducing the value will not adjust prices. When the Minister of Finance spoke in the House of Representatives, the Senate passed a bill to increase the tea tax from 3.54 francs per kilogram to 7.75 francs. The purpose of this move is to protect tea producers in French territories such as Vietnam. (Reuters dispatch on the 20th)

(Paris) The Chamber of Deputies began discussing the budget bill this afternoon. The procedure is to review the entire budget bill without discussing it chapter by chapter. This has been decided by the parliament. Reporter Yager said that the Finance Committee advocates that the budget bill should be completely balanced. The income for this year reached 48,622,000,000 francs, and the initial deficit has been offset. This should be attributed to the various measures taken in the past 20 months. Otherwise, the 1933 budget would have a deficit of 14,000,000,000 francs, and the 1934 budget would have a deficit of 16,000,000,000 francs. The balance of the 1934 budget is indeed a fact. The various measures to reorganize finance are also calculated very practically, and the income estimates are not very high. The reporter also said that in order to maintain the balance of the future budget, we must save expenditures and not allow them to continue to increase, especially railway expenditures. Yager concluded that financial problems are only one aspect of the economic situation. To improve the economy, we must find ways to improve the balance of foreign trade. The discussion point in the Chamber of Deputies immediately shifted to how to maintain the balance of the future budget. Congressman Lelu proposed that expenditures should be tightened and finally said that he would honestly support the government, and members of the right-wing and central parties applauded. Minister of Finance Aman Maddan agreed with this idea and insisted that it is necessary to rationalize railway and land transportation. The budget balance problem should be solved in a comprehensive manner. Domestic and foreign prices should be adjusted, and borrowing interest rates should be reduced. The Minister of Finance also reported that the government will submit a draft law on the financial management of social insurance undertakings, and will also submit a plan for large-scale public works. The general discussion in the Chamber of Deputies then came to an end, and active discussions on the fiscal law began, and the first five articles were passed. The meeting will be held three times tomorrow to continue the discussion in order to complete it quickly. (Havas dispatch on the 20th)

(Paris) Rumors are circulating that the parliament may be dissolved or a "parliamentary recess" may be announced after the budget bill is voted on. Today, the Radical Socialist Party issued a statement declaring that the party has decided to oppose these two measures. The Radical Socialist Party has taken this attitude because it has reached a secret compromise with the opposing right-wing parties, because if a general election is held, it will be very unfavorable to them. (Reuters dispatch on the 20th)

Belgian People Pay Final Respects to the Late King 47

Men, Women, and Children Line Up

Waiting for One Mile From Dawn

Funeral Held, Striving for Simplicity

Brussels: The funeral of the late King of Belgium is scheduled to be held tomorrow. Those who came here from all over the country to offer condolences are like water rushing to a valley. The King's remains are now laid in state in the Imperial Palace. The Belgian people who went to the Palace to pay their final respects to their late King are constantly on the road. Yesterday, late at night, there were still thousands of men, women, and children, lining up for a mile, waiting quietly to pass the Imperial coffin in order. Among them, there were those who came from distant villages and set out before dawn yesterday.

King Albert had expressed his wish before his death that after he reached 100 years old, he should be buried in the Regal Imperial Mausoleum, without any ceremonies. However, the Belgian government now feels it is necessary to hold a state funeral, while the ceremonies should be kept as simple as possible. The Imperial coffin will be moved from the Palace to the Saint Gudule Cathedral tomorrow to sing mass songs, and then moved back to the Regal Imperial Mausoleum for the funeral.

According to a Reuters correspondent in Berlin, President Hindenburg and the German government will be represented by Mr. Keller of the German Ministry of Foreign Affairs to offer condolences in Beijing. It is heard that the former German Crown Prince was eager to attend the ceremony and had signaled to the Belgian government, but the Belgian government did not respond.

Nine aircraft of the British Royal Air Force will escort the Crown Prince from London to Beijing today to represent the British Emperor at the ceremony. The Commander of the Fleet, General Keyes, and an officer of the Royal Air Force, and twenty-five noncommissioned officers will also go to Beijing by sea and land to participate in the funeral. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

(Nanjing) King Albert I of Belgium died in an accident. The funeral will be held on the 22nd. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs telegraphed Zhang Naiyan, the ambassador to Belgium, to send a wreath in the name of the Chairman of the National Government and to represent him in offering condolences. (Special dispatch on the 21st)

Brussels: The Flemish Nationalist members of the Belgian House of Representatives decided not to attend the new King's inauguration ceremony. According to a member, they made this decision because the Flemish nation has nothing to do with the purely Belgian ceremony, and because the Prime Minister praised the late King in the chamber in French instead of Flemish. Political Scandal in Japan: Minister of Education Hatoyama Admits to Receiving Bribes 52

But Believes It Does Not Constitute a Criminal Act

Rumors of 130 Assemblymen Accepting Bribes are Untrue

(Tokyo) Minister of Justice Koyama has submitted the preliminary examination record of Fujita Kozaburo regarding the Sakhalin Industries incident to the Okamoto Investigation Committee through Speaker Akita. The main points are as follows: 230,000 yen was given to Hatoyama in two or three installments of 10,000 yen each, presumably in return for his support of the Seiyukai party. No other money was given to Hatoyama. According to Mori Kaku, as introduced by Hatoyama, 50,000 yen was given to Okamoto Ichiji at the end of January in the third year of Showa [1928] to support the general election. Additionally, 100,000 yen was given to Hamaguchi Yuko through former Sakhalin Governor Masatani Akira, and 50,000 yen was given to Yamamoto Teijiro of the Seiyukai party through Secretary Isaka for election expenses. The above two amounts were paid from the company's logging account. 20,000 yen was given to Isaka in July or August of the third year of Showa, paid from the forestry account. (21st Day, Dentsu Dispatch)

(Tokyo) The Inquiry Committee requested the submission of the prosecutor's investigation documents regarding the Sakhalin Industries incident. Minister of Justice Koyama submitted it to today's Cabinet meeting for publication. It is now clear that Minister of Education Hatoyama received money from Fujita Kozaburo of Sakhalin Industries. However, Minister Hatoyama stated that the money was Fujita's private funds and does not constitute a criminal act. (21st Day, Japan United Dispatch)

Day Three of the Inquiry Committee 53

(Tokyo) The House of Representatives Inquiry Committee investigating Representative Okamoto held its third meeting at 11:10 this morning. Today, due to the publication of evidentiary documents related to the Sakhalin Scandal, the tension at the venue is increasing as the truth regarding Minister Hatoyama's discipline problem is being investigated. Noda Bunjiro of the National Alliance spoke first, saying:

This committee has requested the presence of Railway Minister Mitsuchi, Education Minister Hatoyama, and Finance Minister Takahashi, but they have not attended. What is the reason for this?

Committee Chairman Shimada replied:

The government has notified us that the three ministers will attend the committee at an appropriate time.

Noda then argued that the dispositions of the Japanese artificial silk and Kobe Steel Works incidents were improper and explained in detail the relationship between Kaneko Naokichi, Sumida, and Railway Minister Mitsuchi. Afterwards, Shiga Watari of the Seiyukai party stated:

Representative Okamoto's remarks regarding me are not consistent with the facts. I have never received a report from Minister Hatoyama regarding the handling of the Sakhalin incident. Representative Okamoto's remarks are completely unfounded.

After Shiga finished speaking, Morita Masayoshi of the Seiyukai party demanded that Okamoto retract his words. Next, Taniyama Kohei of the Minseito party stated that every word spoken by Representative Okamoto in the committee is evidence and important material for political judgment. Therefore, he hopes that Representative Okamoto will freely disclose the truth of the incident. He read the verbatim record of Representative Okamoto's speech, which stated that he intended to make it public this year. However, because he was refuting the impromptu remarks of various representatives, he inadvertently revealed those words. When Representative Okamoto was asked what he thought about the bribery incident involving 130 assemblymen last year, Okamoto replied:

There was some regret due to the jeering of many people in the assembly hall and being dominated by the excited atmosphere. However, I was indignant about this issue and suspicious about the source of the current funds for those who notified me of the fact that a large amount of money was distributed. Therefore, I made the notification. I also believe that this matter is a fact. The number of 130 assemblymen may have a few errors, or it may not be known. Taniyama asked:

What kind of reward did Representative Okamoto receive from Minister Hatoyama for the matters handled by Representative Okamoto regarding the Sakhalin incident, which is a very serious criminal case?

Okamoto replied:

I have often been depressed and my state of mind has been very uneasy since this case occurred, but I have never received any reward.

Ueda Kokichi of the Seiyukai party, with a slightly indignant expression, said to Okamoto:

Is there concrete evidence for the distribution of money to 130 Seiyukai assemblymen? Please list the names of the assemblymen.

Okamoto replied:

I cannot disclose them.

At half-past twelve, the chairman announced a recess.

The Inquiry Committee continues to be the focus of public attention. The meeting resumed at 2:15 this afternoon. At that time, Hatoyama Hideo, the Minister of Education's younger brother, was suddenly seen sitting in the audience. First, Fujita Wakasui asked:

Representative Okamoto, as a member of the Seiyukai party, has a pre-existing determination to leave the party in order to expose the wrongdoings of his colleagues. We are very surprised by this action and even have doubts. What is the source of Representative Okamoto's state of mind? Please explain.

Okamoto replied:

Disruption of discipline is very concerning. Therefore, I requested President Suzuki in writing on January 20 to find a way to eliminate discipline.

Fujita then asked:

In the past, Representative Okamoto and Hatoyama jointly committed evidence destruction and repented to take action to eliminate discipline. Is there anything more you are planning to come up with this time?

Okamoto replied:

I have no intention of deliberately harming others.

Fujita claimed:

It is certainly appropriate to crack down on those who disrupt discipline, but it is not appropriate for a warm-blooded human being to ruin the reputation of others without cause. Is the so-called 130 people receiving money from Hatoyama hearsay and an exaggeration?

At this time, Committee Chairman Shimada announced a statement of clarification:

We have just received a letter from Ino Mori, who is from the Seiyukai party (the person Representative Okamoto said he heard it from). Regarding Representative Okamoto's remarks, they are not factual and have already been clarified.

After reading the statement, it is sufficient to prove that what Okamoto said was entirely fictitious. In addition, Yoshiichi Kuboi, who was said to have submitted the diagram, also sent a letter requesting the cancellation of Representative Okamoto's statement and read the letter. The committee members then questioned Okamoto:

Please tell us the names of the people that Representative Okamoto mentioned who had an agreement beforehand and were not convenient to mention.

Next, Takeyasu of the Minseito party requested the submission of documents regarding the disposition of Taiwan Bank stock issues. At this time, Committee Chairman Shimada announced:

The questioning of Representative Okamoto can generally be considered complete. Now we will question Eto Genkuro, but there is very little time left and it can be done next time.

Minister of Justice Koyama also made a brief statement at this time. The meeting was adjourned at 4:05. (21st Day, Japan United Dispatch)

Russo-Japanese Fishing Dispute 55

Russia Declares Japanese Fishing Vote Invalid

(Tokyo) According to a telegram received by the Russian Fisheries Association here at 11:00 PM on the 20th, the Russian side declared that all votes cast by Japanese fishermen in the North Pacific fishing area vote held in Vladivostok on the 20th were invalid. Japanese fishermen first issued Federal National Bank checks at a ratio of 3.225 Japanese yen per ruble to serve as a deposit, with an explanatory note attached during the voting. However, when the Soviet Far East Fisheries Commissioner read the ballots, he declared the votes of the Japanese companies invalid on the grounds that the deposit checks issued by Japanese merchants, calculated according to the National Bank's conversion rate, were less than half of the rent. However, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has not received a public telegram regarding the report of the vote in the Russian-controlled fishing area. Japanese merchants participated in the vote based on the Russo-Japanese Agreement, but the Russian side declared the Japanese merchants' votes invalid and implemented its unilateral vote. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs considers this a violation of the treaty and has decided to issue a strong protest to the Russian government immediately after the public telegram arrives. The content is as follows: (1) The Russian side's unilateral implementation of the vote with a conversion rate of 75 kopecks not only violates the agreement signed by Foreign Minister Kijuhara and Tiranovsky in 1931, but also violates the Russo-Japanese Fisheries Treaty. (2) Japan cannot recognize such an illegal vote result. The Russian side's intention is to take this opportunity to raise the Russo-Japanese exchange rate, but Japan considers this a violation of the treaty and demands its withdrawal. (3) Japan has always insisted on implementing the vote at an exchange rate of 3.225 yen. The Russian side should bear the responsibility for any problems arising from the violation of the treaty. Japan will consider methods of free fishing in Russian territory depending on how the incident develops. (21st Day, Japan United Dispatch)

Another Extreme Cold in the United States 58

Numerous Deaths in New York and Other Places

(New York) The northeastern corner of the United States has recently been hit by strong winds and blizzards. On Monday night, unusually cold weather invaded New York and other places, resulting in numerous deaths. The Soldiers' Memorial in Wilkes-Barre, Pennsylvania, caught fire today. Because all the fire hydrants nearby were frozen, the fire department was unable to extinguish the fire, resulting in the death of ten soldiers' wives and children living in the shelter. New York was hit by wind and snow, and tens of thousands of rural residents with long-term tickets were unable to get to the city to work in time, causing the New York Stock Exchange and the Cotton Exchange to open late at 11:00 AM. Transportation in New Jersey, Massachusetts, and Pennsylvania was disrupted due to the cold and heavy snow. Trains arrived late, and other transportation was also disrupted. New York was hit by a cold wave before November, causing the temperature to drop to 14.5 degrees below zero, breaking a 64-year record. (20th Day, Reuters Dispatch)

(New York) Today, the northeastern and midwestern parts of the United States experienced a sudden cold snap with strong winds and heavy snow, resulting in the deaths of as many as seventeen residents. Transportation in the Northeast was cut off, and all electricity, telephone, and airmail services were suspended. New York City had eight inches of snow, and traffic was obstructed. Over a thousand unemployed workers were temporarily hired to sweep snow and clean streets. (20th Day, National Dispatch)

US Bill to Increase Silver Prices 60

Minting Coins to Promote Trade with China

(Washington) During the discussion of the Silver Bill in the Senate Banking and Currency Committee today, two currency experts strongly argued that using silver as currency would greatly benefit China. Leon, a New York silver expert, said that adopting silver currency would affect the value of Chinese goods and exports, but China would benefit from it soon after because this move could prevent British and Japanese capitalists from controlling Chinese commerce. He also said that this would raise world prices and encourage countries to adopt silver currency. De Longt, a New York statistics expert, agreed to set the ratio of silver to gold at 12 to 1, saying that this is the natural ratio of the two metals. He also said that the United States should mint silver coins similar to Mexican silver dollars, which could also be used in China and could increase US foreign trade, not only with the Far East and China. After the price of silver increases, US trade with China will definitely increase, China's economic situation can gradually become prosperous, and it can purchase foreign goods in large quantities. (20th Day, National Dispatch)

Continued News of British Troops Occupying Yunnan Border 93

More than a Thousand Kawa Soldiers in Ban Hong Area Prepare to Resist

In mid-December of last year, seven or eight British individuals suddenly arrived in the Ban Hong area on the Yunnan border, convened a meeting of local people, and subsequently more than two thousand British troops arrived, bringing equipment and tools to build a motor road. The situation was already reported in yesterday's newspaper, Yunnan News. Now we record the news from the China United Press as follows:

In December of last year, seven or eight British individuals suddenly appeared in the Ban Nong area and convened a secret meeting of the people there. After four or five months of meetings, they dispatched more than two thousand British soldiers, all carrying working tools. Wherever they went, they repaired the roads to make them passable for motor vehicles. They are currently building an iron bridge on the banks of the Ban Nong River. General opinion is that they intend to quickly seize the metals of our Ban Hong. Summarizing the above news, it is confirmed that the British are implementing mining by force. It is now heard that more than a thousand Kawa soldiers have been mobilized in the Ban Hong area to prepare for resistance, and the situation is extremely tense.

The Ban Hong incident is entirely consistent with the past Zhuang Ma negotiations in Jiangxinpo. The area of Meng Gong in Myitkyina, northern Burma under British control, has always produced the world-famous Fei Cui jade. Since the three wonders of Fei Cui at the Chicago Exposition caused a worldwide sensation, it has further aroused the ambitions of the British. Furthermore, it has been found that in the Myitkyina area, in addition to setting up factories to mine gold and jade, the British have also built roads to the banks of the Nujiang River on the Yunnan border in no less than dozens of places. The Nanding River bank already has post roads that directly reach the Yixi Avenue from Kunlian and Dali to Chuxiong in central Yunnan. Even walking to Kunming city would only take five or six days. The British, under the guise of mining, are actually secretly carrying out their important transportation plans. Currently, the disputes in Kangzang (Kham and Tibet), southern Xinjiang, etc., are all related to the British. Our government naturally cannot ignore this negotiation. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs specially appointed Wang Yumei, the Commissioner for Foreign Affairs stationed in Yunnan, to forward a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to Xu Jian, our consul in Yangon (Burmese capital), instructing him to personally inspect the place of illegal mining and assist in the negotiations. Recently, a telegram was received from Li Yuegai, the Director-General of Yixi, which stated, "Commissioner Wang, your telegram is noted. Bian Mi is free to act, and in fact there is nothing to be done. However, no matter which line, we have the right to speak within the undetermined border (omitted). As for the location of the Maolong factory at that time, most were in Ban Hong, and some were within the current jurisdiction of Gengma. The detailed sections of the yellow line's passage are difficult to investigate suddenly. In addition to urgently ordering the Zhenkang county magistrate to supervise Gengma Guisi in a detailed investigation, drawing, and reporting, I respectfully reply. I pray that it be presented to the Chairman for review, and I request a telegram to Director-General Yang to instruct Shuangjiang and Lancang to supervise Mengjiao Dong, Xijian, Mengda, and other Tusi to investigate and report. Your younger brother Li Yuegai (31st) seal." (China United

General Situation of Huluwang Area 94

(Li Jingsen)

Yesterday's important news reported the alarm of British troops invading the Yunnan border. The true nature of the content is not yet fully known. However, the perilousness of the Yunnan border has long been noted by people in Yunnan. The Fudian Bank sent Mr. Li Jingsen to the Huluwang area last year (1933) in January to investigate the mining area situation. According to his report upon returning to the province, the area occupies one-sixth of the entire Yunnan province and has rich reserves. Foreigners have coveted it for a long time. It is related to national defense and mining in every way, and our country should promptly plan for its development. Then the importance of the problem can be known. We Chinese only know that the Northeast has Huludao, but we do not know that the Southwest has the even more important Huluwang area. Now we specifically look for and record Mr. Li's investigation of the general situation as follows:

Introduction 95

Since the success of the Northern Expedition, especially after the September 18th Incident, more and more Chinese people have paid attention to border construction. From the perspective of the country's future, can this not be called a good phenomenon? However, the vision of the Chinese people is not comprehensive, paying attention to the Northwest but not to the Southwest, especially not valuing Yunnan, which is located between the two. Moreover, considering the situation of the Yunnan border, the general public also has biases, only knowing about the loss of Jiangxinpo and Pianma, but not knowing that the Huluwang area, which is located in the southwest, has fallen into a dangerous state. It is also a region rich in mineral products and fertile land, which cannot but be regretted.

The Huluwang area originally had upper and lower divisions. The Ban Kuang and other places belonging to the lower Huluwang were, due to the ignorance of the authorities, allowed to be划歸 in the border agreement and are now only the upper Huluwang area. It is located in the southwestern corner of the province, northwest of Gongming Mountain, bordering British Burma to the west, Shuangjiang to the east, Mengding and Gengma to the north, and Lancang and Menglian to the south. The area is thousands of square miles, with a population of nearly one million. The climate is mild, the soil is fertile, and the products are abundant, especially gold and silver mineral products. However, the people have very low awareness, are ignorant and confused, know nothing of the outside world, still eat raw meat and drink blood, and even live in caves and wilderness, remaining in a primitive state.

The Huluwang area is currently divided and governed by five kings, namely Ban Hong, Shui Bang, Ban Lao, Kwong Bie, and Shao Xing, with King Shao Xing as the chief king. The area has always belonged to our country. At the end of the Han Dynasty, Kongming's southern expedition and the Ming Dynasty's Wang Ji's expedition to Burma both reached this country with their power and virtue. Even after hundreds of years, the people still worship Kongming and Wang Ji. During the Qianlong period of the Qing Dynasty, the government established formal and deputy magistrates to govern the area. At the same time, Wu Shangxian from Shiping went to Ban Hong to open the Maolong Silver Factory, and Gongli Yan went to Ban Kuang to mine the Laoyin Factory, both of which achieved great success. Later, due to poor politics, it was advisable to report failure. As of today, Ban Kuang is owned by the British, and the old silver factory has been mined using new methods, while Maolong is still abandoned. During the Qianlong period, due to the mining relationship, the relationship between the Huluwang area and the hinterland of the province can be said to be the closest. Unfortunately, the government at that time lacked vision and failed to timely implement political education and guide the people of the area. In the twelfth year of Guangxu (1886), Burma fell to the British, and the Huluwang area became one of the border lands, and its position became increasingly important. In the twenty-eighth year of the Qing Dynasty, the Governor-General of Yunnan and Guizhou, Wang Wenshao, and the Finance Commissioner, Liu Chunlin, summoned the King of Ban Hong to the province, bestowed clothing and other items, and explained the government's kindness, ordering him to return to his homeland to guard it. Later, when unrest occurred in the area, Peng Yaonan (from Mianning) was ordered to garrison the area for many years and was deeply respected by the five kings and the people. His prestige still exists today. Since the Republic of China, the government has not forgotten to be kind to distant lands and has sent officials several times to express condolences, but those sent were not always suitable, not only failing to fulfill their missions but also having a bad influence on the border people. The civilization of the Huluwang area has not yet begun, which is truly regrettable. No matter from the historical, ethnic, or other aspects, there is no doubt that the area should belong to our country. However, the British, knowing its abundant mineral resources and excellent land, coveted it and, in the twenty-fifth year of Guangxu, when surveying the border, claimed that the latitude and longitude of Xuetou did not match the treaty, forcibly designated Kongming Mountain as Gongming Mountain, and drew a red line on another map, penetrating more than a hundred miles into our interior. According to the British map, not only would the Huluwang area not belong to us, but also Maoshou, Ximeng, Guangman Nong, and other places belonging to Lancang would also belong to the British, resulting in significant losses for our side. The request was immediately rejected, and it remains a pending issue to this day. However, over these decades, British aggression has been continuous. They have sent personnel to secretly observe the situation in the area at any time. Their most coveted object is the Maolong silver mine, because not only are the mineral reserves abundant, but even the tailings have thick profits to be made. In the eighth year of the Republic of China, the Ban Kuang British Burma Silver Mining Company moved merchants to come and buy the mine tailings, paying as much as ten British dollars per hundred catties. If the ore was not of excellent quality, they would not have offered such a price. Fortunately, the local people were loyal to the Han and did not please the British, so they immediately stopped it. Although they wanted to invade, they suffered from having no way. However, although the local people rejected the British and leaned towards the Han, the Hui people in Ban Nong were willing to be lackeys and serve as vanguards, invading internally, which is also a major crisis in the five kings' territories. It is said that the Hui people in Ban Nong migrated here during the Du Wenxiu era. The area is under the jurisdiction of King Ban Lao, who married the Hui people's Ma Wanquan as his son-in-law. Gradually, the king's power fell to the side, and when Ma's son Bicang arrived, he even drove the king out and seized his position, calling himself the Ban Nong official. The area borders British Burma, and the economic relationship between the two places is very close, so the Hui people are mostly lured by the British, forgetting their ancestors and willing to be the dogs of the British, standing in opposition to the five kings. In the seventh year of the Republic of China, the Hui people in Ban Nong plotted to attack the five kings, but fortunately, Peng Yaonan, the commander of the Lancang border defense camp, stopped them. If our side does not increase its border defense forces in the future, then a large-scale internal attack by the Hui people is a foreseeable event.

The author lives in Mianning, close to the area, and is deeply aware of the border crisis. He constantly thinks of ways to serve the country. Moreover, because Mr. Peng Yaonan, whose reputation shook the five kings, has a family relationship with the author, he has a deep connection with the local people and has his own efforts. In the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, he was ordered by the Department of Agriculture and Mining to investigate mineral products. After several months of trekking, he was able to return to the province to report. In January of this year (1933), he was again ordered by the Fudian New Bank to negotiate mineral products and announce the government's kindness. It took several months to complete his mission. The author believes that the territory governed by the five kings is important and the situation is special, but the country is still unaware of the situation there. Therefore, while investigating and negotiating mineral affairs, he also conducted general inspections in the general situation, hoping to contribute what he gained to society, to solve the mystery of the Chinese people, and to help develop the border areas. However, the author has shallow academic knowledge and has not conducted thorough investigations, so he is bound to be guilty of hanging one and missing ten. I hope that those who know will teach me.

1. Natural Conditions 96

A. People (1) Population: There are approximately one million people. Because the area is close to the tropics, the climate is mild, and the products are abundant, the population is multiplying rapidly. For example, the weather is better and the products are more abundant in King Shao Xin's territory (i.e., Shao Xing), and the population increase is greater than in the territories of other kings, about 500,000. King Ban Hong's territory has about 300,000. Others, such as the three indigenous territories of Ban Lao, Yong Ban (i.e., Yong Bang), and Kuang Bie, each have 50,000 to 60,000 people. They all live scattered in the mountains, living a life of semi-agriculture and semi-hunting. (2) Ethnicity: The people of the area are the descendants of the San Miao, Jiu Li, Jing Man, and Nan Man in ancient times, and are also one of the Mongolian races. The Pu Man people of the Miao ethnic group are divided into all territories and are named Kawa. They have square faces, long necks, yellow-brown skin, and are simple in nature, truly possessing the air of ancient barbaric peoples, the same as the lives of the primitive people described in history. (3) Nature: The nature of the people is straightforward, simple, stubborn, and dull, and progress is very slow. Moreover, because they like hunting, they have developed a cruel nature. No one dares to associate with them, and an extremely large gap has been drawn between them and the Han people, reducing the opportunity for civilization.

B. Land (1) Location: It is located on the southwestern border of the province, bordering Shuangjiang to the east, Lancang and Menglian to the south, Gengma and Mengding to the north, and British Burma to the west. It is located in the center of travel between China and Burma, and is truly an important town in Yunnan. (2) Area: The area is approximately thousands of square miles, extending a thousand miles east-west and more than seven hundred miles north-south, accounting for almost one-sixth of Yunnan. Shao Xin has about 5,000 square miles, Ban Hong has about 2,000 square miles, Kuang Bie has 2,000 square miles, and Ban Lao and Yong Ban each have more than 1,000 square miles. (3) Terrain: Gongming Mountain connects to the remaining force of the Nushan Mountains, dominating the center, reaching a height of approximately 7,000 meters. Branches divide into five lines, mutually connected and surrounding the Black Mountain in the eastern part of Shao Xin. The Black Mountain branches westward, stretching more than seven hundred miles, directly entering Jinchangba, connecting to the mountains rich in gold and silver minerals. The northern branch of the mountains runs northward, connecting to the Sanjianshan of Gengma. The entire territory forms a large plateau. The mountain terrain is rugged, extending for thousands of miles. To the east of Gongming Mountain are the Nanka River and the Nanlei River, which flow into Burma. The water is turbulent and inconvenient for boats. To the west is the Salween River, which also flows into Burma. To the north are the Nanding River and the Gunlong River, which flow into the Salween River. The water is turbulent and the terrain is dangerous.

C. Climate: The area is located within 13 degrees north latitude and has entered the tropics. However, because the mountains extend horizontally, towering into the clouds, and the terrain is uneven, it has both cold, warm, and hot climates. In the plains and deep valleys, the terrain is low, the climate is hot, and there is also a lot of humidity. The miasma is particularly severe. The mountainous areas have a mild air, much like a temperate zone. As for the high mountains, they are often covered with snow and are very cold. As for storms and mists, they often occur due to the terrain.

D. Transportation: Because of the towering mountains that extend horizontally and the dense forests that block the sun, and also because there is little contact with outsiders, there is no way to talk about road construction. Therefore, the roads are rugged and winding like sheep intestines, making it difficult for people and horses to pass through, and transportation is very difficult. Although there are many rivers, because the terrain is uneven and the water flows rapidly, they are inconvenient for navigation and can only be used by the local people for fishing.

E. Minerals: (1) Metallic minerals: The area's metallic minerals are particularly abundant, with the best quality. It is as if every mountain has them and every place has them. It can be considered the best gold and silver area in the country. It is described in detail below. (Silver mine) The silver mine is produced west of the Black Mountain and under the Great Tip Mountain, at the junction of the three kings of Ban Hong, Ban Lao, and Yong Ban. The mining area is more than a hundred miles north-south and seventy or eighty miles east-west. The mineral veins are accumulated, and the mountains are all covered. Every year, erosion caused by wind and rain flows into the streams. If a mountain valley collapses and mineral rocks appear, it is truly inexhaustible. The quality of the ore is very good. In the old days, the British stole it for analysis, and they also said that the quality of the ore was very good. It is a pity that such abundant mineral veins and good quality ore are abandoned on the ground. (Gold mine) The gold mine is produced between King Shao Xin and the Black Mountain. There is a river in the mountains, containing a lot of gold sand, flowing directly into Jinchangba. The river is also named Jinsha River because it produces gold sand. Every year, the prince allows the people to pan for gold sand for three days, which can cover half a year's expenses. The abundance of gold mines can also be imagined. Other minerals such as copper, iron, antimony, tin, and nickel are found everywhere and are common throughout the area. It is truly an area rich in gold, silver, and treasures. Unfortunately, the government has not paid attention to development and cannot make the best use of its land. (2) Non-metallic minerals: In addition to the abundant metallic minerals, Ban Hong also has particularly abundant non-metallic minerals. For example, the coal mine is produced west of Jinchangba, and the mining area stretches for hundreds of miles. The local people have a lot of firewood and grass, so they have not yet used it. There are also particularly many other raw materials of various kinds. As for gemstones, they are colorful, dazzling, and even unseen by people in the interior.

F. Animals: Because Ban Hong is close to the tropics and has a mild climate, all kinds of animals are particularly strong compared to the interior. Both domestic and wild animals are tall and fat. Domestic and wild animals are described separately below. (1) Domestic animals: Because people live a life of semi-agriculture and semi-pastoralism, they also raise many domestic animals. They are divided into two types according to their nature: 1. Those who live with people: there are chickens, dogs, and pigs. Chickens account for 7 percent, dogs account for 1 percent, and pigs account for 6 percent. They are directly raised by people with wheat, dry rice, corn, etc., and kept in the house. 2. Those who do not live with people: there are yellow cattle, water buffalo, sheep, goats, horses, mules, and donkeys. Yellow cattle are the most numerous, accounting for 25 percent of the total. Water buffalo account for 8 percent, goats account for 20 percent, sheep account for 10 percent, horses account for 10 percent, mules account for 10 percent, and donkeys account for 10 percent. Although the above animals are domestic animals, they are similar to wild animals, eating and sleeping in the mountains day and night, no different from wild beasts. When people want to use them, they hunt them like wild beasts. (2) Wild animals: The various wild animals are also tropical products, such as elephants, tigers, leopards, bears, deer, muntjac, wild donkeys, wild cattle, wild boars, etc. Elephants are produced in both Ban Hong and Yong Ban, totaling more than 20. Tigers, leopards, bears, etc., often appear day and night along the riverbanks. As for deer, muntjac, wild cattle, and wild boars, they are found everywhere, and people hunt them for food. There are also birds such as peacocks, pheasants, parrots, and mandarin ducks, with beautiful feathers and bright colors, strange and varied, and many kinds.

G. Plants: (1) Trees: The plants in the area are mostly tropical products, different from those in the interior. The trees in the deep mountains are more than ten feet in circumference and several dozen feet in height. There are countless such large trees everywhere on the mountains. The types are complex and difficult to enumerate. Among them, the most famous are the Lei tree, Jiujiang, Zibai, Na Lei Lei, Zhuang, Zhao, etc., which grow the fastest, growing one foot per year and one foot wide. In the deep valleys, there are also large bean trees and crow pillow trees, which are also particularly tall. The local people take their fruits as food. The shell is like a box, which can hold things and be used as children's toys. (2) Fruit trees: The most notable fruit trees are loquats, grapes, sesame plum fruits, yellow fruits, bananas, etc., which taste extremely sweet, fragrant, and delicious, but they are all wild and rarely cultivated. There are no other peaches, plums, apricots, etc. (3) Flowers and grasses: Strange flowers and exotic herbs are found everywhere in the area. The flowers are mostly beautiful and large, and there are many kinds. Those who see them are amazed. There are even fresh flowers that do not wither all year round, which are even rarer in the interior. There are many kinds of grasses, too numerous to mention. The most famous are the three kinds: fragrant grass, Zhanjian grass, and large batch grass, which are extremely lush. The stems are as large as cups, and the leaves are juicy, making it easy to fatten livestock when used to feed them. (4) Grains: The main grains are dry rice and corn, followed by wheat and millet. Planting here is simple and harvests are abundant. Every year in February, trees are cut down and burned after they are dry, and then planted, sprouting immediately without weeding. By May or June, a good harvest can be obtained.

2. Economic Conditions 97

A. Agriculture: The climate is mild and the soil is fertile in the Huluwang area, making agriculture easy. However, because people live a semi-nomadic life, they focus on livestock and hunting, and planting is only a subordinate activity. Livestock and hunting are the main activities. The local agricultural conditions are described below. (1) Planting: Due to the climate and geography, planting with simple cultivation can yield a good harvest. The main crops are dry rice, corn, millet, and wheat. The planting method is to first cut down trees and dense weeds in January each year, expose them to the sun, and then burn them with fire. With a little manual labor, the soil is loosened, and the seeds are sown on them in March. Without weeding, it is possible to obtain a bumper harvest from July to August. Planting by one person can easily provide for several people. Therefore, most local people do not take planting as their main occupation. Annual agricultural products can only meet needs, with little surplus. Moreover, the people are under the oppression of the various kings, and the taxes are very heavy. The surplus of planting is all collected. Also, whenever planting is done, the people must gather to finish the planting of the prince before they can plant their own. Therefore, the general people do not have time to cultivate and are unwilling to do much planting. Therefore, although they are located in places with good climate and soil, farming is declining. (2) Animal husbandry: The climate is hot and the trees and grasses are flourishing, and because the mountains are horizontal and the forests are dense, animal husbandry is particularly developed. Both cattle, sheep, horses, donkeys, mules, etc., are produced in large quantities. The people use them as their main food, and many are also exported. However, the livestock in a certain king's territory are exclusively owned by the king, and no one else can enter the territory to hunt them. Even what his people eat is bestowed by the king. The people cannot own them privately. Livestock in all regions often live and reproduce in the mountains, similar to wild animals. This is truly using the earth as a large pasture. (3) Hunting: In addition to planting and animal husbandry, the main occupation of the people is hunting. When work is completed, whether men or women, they take knives, guns, nets, and spears to hunt birds and beasts in the mountains or fish by the water. From the prince to the people, everyone likes to engage in this activity, so they have developed a cruel nature.

B. Industry: The people in the area still live in the primitive age. Also, because animals are abundant and clothing, food, and housing are easily resolved, there is no need to seek other ways of making a living, and industry is naturally out of the question. The only industries now are extremely simple handicrafts, such as weaving hemp and bamboo. Among them, the only notable industry is a kind of hemp fabric called Kawa Bei Lei, which is six feet long and three feet wide. The construction is very simple. The local people wear it on their bodies as clothing. As for the various tools they use, they are all purchased from the Han people in the border areas. Their industry is still stagnating in the primitive state.

C. Commerce: Because transportation is not available and the customs are barbaric, outsiders mostly do not dare to go deep into the area, only trading in the border areas. Commerce in the area is very sparse. The various situations are described below. 1. External trade: Every year, there are two seasons, in March and October. The people go out to the Tusi lands of Gengma, Mengjiao Dong, Mengdian, and the British Burmese border area of Maliba, and trade with Han people, Hui people, Burmese, Baiyi Bennong, etc. The main exports are opium, Zigeng, etc. They mostly do not use weighing scales, but estimate with the eye, which is very simple. They are very trustworthy when trading with people. If they order goods from people, they use wood carvings as proof. Even after several years, if they meet again, the ordered goods, no matter how decayed, are still preserved. This is truly "keeping one's word." The intermediaries in foreign trade are mostly currencies, including French silver dollars, British silver dollars, and Chinese silver dollars. In recent years, the various kings have absorbed a lot of silver coins, but they are rarely used, so they are mostly buried underground. 2. Internal trade: Because Han people mostly do not dare to go deep into the area, only pure local people enter the area to trade. Also, because there are no markets, trading can take place anywhere between villages. By means of bartering, they exchange salt, tea, oil, sugar, cloth fabrics, grass fabrics, iron and copper utensils, etc., for the opium, Zigeng, and livestock they produce. Internal trade is mostly done by women, who are very trustworthy and fair. The procedures are also very simple, completely a primitive social life, an era of bartering.

Three Aspects of Life 98

一. Language: Within the territory, the people are of pure ethnicity, with very few people of different ethnicities intermingling. Therefore, the language is still relatively unified. Although there are slight differences, they are only the differences between "cooked barbarian language" (熟蕃語) and "raw barbarian language" (生蕃語). Below is a comparison of how they pronounce numbers:

Chinese: (一) (二) (三) (四) (五) (六) (七) (八) (九) (十)

Cooked Barbarian Language: Di, La, Lü, Peng, Bing, Nai, Qiao, Dai, Dian, Gao

Raw Barbarian Language: Ti, La, Li, Ben, Mian, Leng, Ye, Tai, Tian, Ke

Judging from the above, the two types of barbarian language, cooked and raw, are quite similar. The distinction between clear and muddy sounds is not very significant. The language commonly used within the territory and for communication with outsiders is mainly the cooked barbarian language. If outsiders wish to enter the territory, they must learn this language, or they cannot enter. Furthermore, because there is no written script, it is difficult for outsiders to learn. This is also a major reason for the lack of progress.

B. Customs: (1) Marriage: There is no strict distinction in bloodlines. Except for direct siblings, marital relations are not allowed. However, cousins within the family can freely marry anyone. Regardless of gender, when they reach the age of 17 or 18, they dance and sing together. If they are compatible, they engage in physical relations. Therefore, it is very common for children to be born before they become formally married. After engaging in physical relations, if the man and woman are fond of each other and reluctant to part, the man will first hide the woman elsewhere before asking a companion (i.e., a matchmaker from inland China) to explain the situation to the woman's family. If permission is granted, they first gather together and have tea as an engagement ceremony. Only after having children do they formally marry, with a meat-eating feast as the ceremony. At the wedding, guests from both the bride and groom's families bring one or two taels of meat as gifts. Everyone sits around and eats the meat they brought before stopping. In this way, they become a formal couple. This is truly free-love marriage. (2) Funerals: Funeral ceremonies are very simple. When someone dies, it is believed to be because Heaven cannot tolerate them, and others are afraid of being implicated. The deceased is buried immediately and not left for a long time. After a person dies, they are wrapped in a bamboo curtain and buried in the ground. There are no other procedures or sacrificial rites. (3) Social Interaction: People mostly use wooden carvings as proof of agreements. Whether buying and selling land or engaging in other transactions, wooden carvings are used instead of contracts. For example, if Person A buys land from Person B, a piece of wood is carved with patterns and shapes of birds and beasts, about five inches long. It is split in half; the seller burns half publicly to permanently cut off ties, and the buyer keeps the other half as a contract. This method is also used for transactions; each party keeps half as proof. When they meet later, they can recognize each other. Therefore, all kinds of social interactions rely on this as evidence, gradually becoming a custom.

C. Religion: (1) Animism: The territory has towering terrain and dense forests. The people live by farming and hunting; hence, they mostly worship mountains, rivers, trees, and forests. Each village has a large forest of trees called "Dragon Trees." The natives are not allowed to take anything from the Dragon Trees. If they accidentally take something and become ill, they believe it is because the Dragon Trees are causing trouble. Every year, during the spring and autumn seasons, on the day of the Tiger in the lunar calendar, they slaughter cattle or sheep as a sacrifice. For five days from the day of the sacrifice, no one is allowed to pass through the Dragon Bridge, to show avoidance and prevent offending the gods. (2) Ghost Worship: Ghost worship is also known as "Doing Ghosts." When people become ill, they believe it is because ghosts are causing trouble. They invite about ten people who can "Do Ghosts" to the riverbank or roadside, where they kneel on the ground on behalf of the sick person. Everyone chants incantations, scatters rice in all directions, says words of telling the ghosts what they want, and sacrifices a cow and a sheep as offerings. (3) Offering to the Harvest: Every year during the spring and autumn seasons, when planting and harvesting grains, people send others out to capture the heads of Han Chinese and Bai Yi people to sacrifice to the harvest. The more heads, the better, especially those with long beards and hair. If it is difficult to capture outsiders, wild indigenous people also come to the border to capture pure indigenous people as sacrifices. Therefore, few people interact with them during the spring and autumn seasons. During the sacrifice, the heads are impaled on long poles and planted in the dry-land grain fields. The nearby people are summoned, and each person brings tea, rice, silver, etc., to offer as a sacrifice. Everyone kneels and cries, stuffing the things they brought into the mouths of the heads, crying and saying, "You came to our place to find money and rice, but you were killed to sacrifice to the dry-land grain. You cannot eat or see your parents, wife, and friends, so we give you more money and rice to eat. We hope you ascend to heaven and bless our dry-land grain to have a bumper harvest." After the sacrifice, the heads are taken to other places for sacrifice. If other places also kill heads and bring them back, they are left for wild animals to eat, to signify that the heads have ascended to heaven, and it is hoped that the dry-land grain will have a bumper harvest. This cruel sacrifice has become an unchangeable custom. (4) Other: Recently, in some areas near Burma, temples have been built, and Buddhism is revered, which has a certain impact on local culture. In recent years, British missionaries have been sent to the border areas to learn the local language and deeply propagate their faith. Some people also worship them. This is something that deserves close attention.

D. Education: The people in this territory are savage and do not know what education is. Only a few young masters and princes from the aristocratic families within the territory of Ban Hong Wang request monks from the border areas to teach them a few scriptures.

E. Lifestyle: (1) Clothing: Clothing is mostly made of rough and simple cloth woven from cotton or hemp. Only pure indigenous people sew them into clothing to cover their bodies. As for the wild indigenous people, they are mostly naked, with their bodies painted black. Regardless of gender, they only use one or two chi [unit of measurement] to cover their genitals, which is extremely unsightly and no different from beasts. (2) Diet: Food is mostly eaten raw. Although pure indigenous people have recently learned to cook slightly, they only casually heat it through. As for the wild indigenous people, they do not know how to cook. They eat raw rice and raw meat, rarely cooking it before eating. What is even stranger is that meat must be left until it has a rancid smell to be considered delicious and fragrant. The main foods are dry-land grain, corn, millet, ginger, and chili peppers. They are particularly fond of tea and wine. Regardless of wealth, they drink tea five or six times a day, several bowls each time. They are addicted to alcohol as if it were their life. They often form groups and go to the lands of Gengma, Mengjiao, Dong, and other local leaders to trade for wine and food. They can be seen drunk and lying on the ground everywhere. As for drinking raw sheep and raw cow blood, or splashing blood on rice and eating it, it makes people want to vomit. Their bodies are healthy, and their resistance is strong, perhaps due to their lifestyle. (3) Housing: Because the climate is hot, they cannot live on flat land. Houses are mostly built on high mountains, and the style is extremely simple. They are all thatched huts. Those built in the style of pavilions are commonly called "Zhan Lou". Those built on the ground are called "thatched sheds". If the roof has two planks protruding one chi long, it indicates that it is their royal residence. Other common people cannot imitate this. Houses are scattered all over the mountains, rarely clustered together. (4) Sleep: Regardless of princes or commoners, they set up a fireplace in the middle of the house. At night, they sleep together without any separation. Parents, brothers, sisters, wives, all huddle around the fireplace and sleep together. Therefore, there are many cases of murder and incest in the territory.

Four Political Conditions 99

A. Social Organization: Although the people in the territory are still in a nomadic stage, without capitalists or landlords, there is already a class division between nobles and commoners. The rulers are the oppressing class. People of all classes must absolutely obey the ruling class; otherwise, the upper class has the power to execute them. The social organization is illustrated below:

Great Prince - Each Prince - Each Grain Leader

Each Head of Household - Each Centurion - Each

Manager - People

From this, we can see the large number of classes and the heavy oppression suffered by the people. Whenever people encounter members of the upper class, they must perform the kowtow ceremony. The strictness of the upper class is imaginable.

B. Political Implementation: (1) Political Power: Political power is held in the hands of the various princes. Within their respective territories, matters of finance, military preparations, trials, punishments, rewards, issuing orders, etc., are not to be interfered with by others and are entirely in the hands of the princes. Moreover, the princes are hereditary, and the people are slaves for generations. As for the relationship between each prince and the Overall Prince (i.e., the Shaoxing Prince), other than paying tribute once every three years, there is nothing else. (2) Political Decrees: Because there is no written script, when princes want to implement political decrees within the territory, and when people want to report matters, they rely on wooden carvings as proof. Regardless of rest, as long as there is an order from a superior or when encountering a superior leader, they must perform the most respectful kowtow ceremony. When there is an emergency in the territory that requires summoning all the people, they blow a cow horn as the command to gather the people. (To be continued)

Sun Did Not Accept Advice from Pang Bingxun and Others 100

Jin-Sui Army Has Received 300,000 Yuan in Departure Funds

Beiping Correspondence: Regarding the disposition of Sun Dianying's troops, since Military Commission members Pang Bingxun, Ji Yiqiao, and Hu Yukun sent a final telegram to Sun with advice, no reply has been received from Sun as of tonight (the 20th). It is generally speculated that the effectiveness of the advice telegram will be extremely limited, so a peaceful resolution will ultimately become a pipe dream. Observing Sun's troops' recent active attacks on Pingluo, it is clear that Sun has no sincerity for peace. Furthermore, since Sun sent Jin Zunhua to Beiping, he has repeatedly convened meetings of officers above the rank of regimental commander at Fangci to discuss future prospects. His direct-line officers generally advocated that Sun not leave hastily, expressing a willingness to share hardships. Sun originally did not want to leave the army and now uses the excuse that his subordinates have expressed this sentiment, making it even more difficult to accept the advice of Pang and others. Therefore, Pang and others are keeping the original telegram strictly confidential, not wanting to disclose it to the outside world to avoid seeking embarrassment. Jin Zunhua, who came to Beiping in response to He Yingqin's telegram summons, has no choice but to wait for Sun's reply to determine his next course of action, given that Beiping has already sent an advisory telegram. However, he plans to stay in Beiping for the time being.

Ningsia Chairman Ma Hongkui sent a telegram to Beiping today, forwarded by Deng Baoshan in Gansu. The general idea was to inquire about the situation of the Jin-Sui Army and urge Xu Fu and others to quickly advance their troops to relieve the siege of Ningsia Province. Currently, Sun's troops around Pingluo are concentrating their forces to fiercely attack. The various forts outside Ningsia City are still occupied by Sun's troops. Ma Baolin's troops inside the city are putting up a valiant resistance. There have been daily contacts near Ningsia's new city. Sun Dianying himself is traveling back and forth to command in the vicinity of the Great and Small Mosques and has established a puppet provincial government in Shizuizi, replacing the magistrates and tax bureau and public security bureau chiefs of Dengkou and Pingluo counties. It is said that Sun is preparing to flee to eastern Gansu and join forces with Xu bandits in northern Sichuan when the Jin-Sui Army moves out.

The Jin-Sui Army units that have been dispatched, Zhao Chengzhou's cavalry and the two brigades of Tian Shumei and Wang Deying under Wang Jingguo's command, have all arrived in Linhe. Follow-up units such as Wang Shu'an's cavalry division are also preparing to move out. Zhao Chengzhou himself arrived in Suiyuan today (the 20th), will stay briefly, and then go to Baotou and transfer to Linhe to arrange everything. Wang Shu'an is also going to Suiyuan to meet with Wang Jingguo. The Dong and Zhang brigades of Fu Zuoyi's troops will also successively move west starting today. The infantry and artillery are transported by car after passing Baotou, which is extremely short of cars, so the advance is inevitably slower. It is said that the Military Commission will allocate a number of military transport vehicles to facilitate military transport. The General Directorate of Military Stations will be established in Baotou in the future. All the Jin-Sui troops departing will temporarily gather in Linhe, awaiting orders to advance west.

The Gan-Ning armies plan to encircle Sun's troops. Ningxia and Pingluo will continue to be defended by the troops of Ma Hongbin and Ma Hongkui. After the Jin-Sui Army completes its deployment, they will launch an attack. A unit of Ma Bufang's division has arrived at Honggangshan, planning to outflank Sun's army. The Gan-Ning border defense is extremely solid, with a force of 30,000 troops at Zhongwei.

Xu Yongchang and Fu Zuoyi have been in Beiping for several days, discussing military expenses with He Yingqin. A result has been reached. He has agreed to allocate approximately 300,000 yuan for the first month's military expenses and rations for the 41st Army to the Jin-Sui Army. Yesterday, 50,000 yuan in cash was received from the Military Commission and remitted to the principal. Fu Zuoyi will be able to set off in one or two days after the cost of establishing the supply station is calculated. Fu hosted a banquet for the members of the Military Commission at his private residence this afternoon. The above issues were further discussed after the banquet. Furthermore, it is reported that after the central government sent Zhang Tingmeng and others to drive the Air Administration's 401 and 402 aircraft to Lanzhou, Zhu Shaoliang immediately sent them to work in the Ningsia provincial capital. On the 10th of this month, the two aircraft carried a large number of leaflets entitled "A Loyal Admonition to the Soldiers of the 15th Route Army, 35th Division, 9th Division, and 2nd Cavalry Division of Qinghai and Ningsia Provinces to the Entire 41st Army" and flew to Sun's troops' positions on the outskirts of the city to scatter them, urging them to quickly come to their senses. After scattering them, they flew back to Lanzhou. Due to weather conditions, they have not continued to fly there in recent days (the 20th).

Gubeikou Will Be Taken Over 101

Date Has Been Set for the 28th

Japanese Troops and Puppet Organizations Will Withdraw Slowly

We Will Only Take Over Administrative Power

Beiping Correspondence: It has been over eight months since Gubeikou fell. Through the recent efforts of Huang Fu, Yin Rugeng, and others to negotiate with the Japanese, it has been decided to take over on the 28th. Looking at the negotiation process, since last November, Yin once went to Gubeikou to negotiate with Japanese representatives. At that time, it was rumored that the takeover could be expected by the end of the year, but it was delayed because the details of the takeover could not be finalized. Recently, after Yuguan decided to take over, the Japanese also urged us to proceed with the takeover negotiations for Gubeikou as soon as possible. Yin was ordered to come to Beiping and first asked the Zhenzheng Hui Huang Fu for instructions, then went to Tianjin to conduct a concrete study with the Hebei Provincial Government. The takeover plan and details were completely determined. He then returned to Beiping from Tianjin and had detailed discussions with Japanese Embassy military attaché Shibayama. A few days ago, Shibayama telegraphed Matsui, the acting head of the Japanese Special Agency stationed in Chengde, to set a date to conduct takeover procedures with our representatives. Matsui telegraphed back from Changchun, saying that he could arrive in Gubeikou on the 24th or 25th, and requested Yin Rugeng and others to go there for negotiations. To save procedures, Yin asked Shibayama yesterday (the 19th) to telegraph Matsui, asking him to handle the handover matters together. The Japanese have already agreed to most of the details, so there should be no problems. Therefore, Yin is currently preparing for the takeover procedures and has set the 25th to go to Gubeikou with the takeover personnel to have a discussion with Matsui. On the 26th and 27th, both parties will prepare the procedures. On the 28th, the official takeover will take place. The handover ceremony will be the same as the takeover of Shanhaiguan. In addition to Yin Rugeng, the takeover personnel include the director of the Zuo Zhi Bureau, the director of the Gubeikou Office of the Jiji Administrative Commissioner's Office, and the director of the Gubeikou Public Security Bureau. The provincial government has appointed Liu Youdong and Huo Shi as the director of the Gubeikou Zuo Zhi Bureau and the director of the office. The candidate for the director of the Public Security Bureau has not been determined and will be announced soon. Matsui will supervise the handover by the Japanese. Yesterday, Yin sent personnel to Gubeikou to make preparations. This afternoon, Yin left Beiping and returned to his residence in Tongzhou to handle everything. This time, the administrative power of Gubeikou will be taken over first. Military and political power will have to wait a bit. The Japanese troops in Gubeikou are using the excuse that there are no barracks outside the port and will not withdraw for the time being. They must wait until the barracks are repaired before they can be transferred. All the puppet organizations will not be moved and withdrawn for a while and will temporarily be mixed with our organizations. The Japanese also requested restrictions on the number of police and security teams stationed in Gubeikou and the number of guns, intending that it should not exceed 500 people. Police officers on duty must not carry guns. Our side still disagrees with this point and must negotiate again during the takeover. As for the establishment of customs, which concerns finance, personnel will be sent by the Ministry of Finance to carry out the work after the takeover. The various ports of Malan峪 are also preparing to be taken over (February 20).

Songjiang

Provincial Order Designates Clearance Measurement to Be Handled 102

Last year, the Provincial Land Bureau commissioned a triangular root point team to come to Songjiang to survey the location and set up markers to measure the triangulation points for future clearance measurement. Now, the county government has received instructions from the provincial government that the Land Bureau intends to implement the administrative guidelines for the second half of the 22nd year, planning to start clearance measurement in nine counties, including Changshu, Songjiang, and Shanghai, because the measurement by the root point team in each county is sufficient for clearance measurement, and the funds for clearance measurement are assessed with a certain percentage, which is sufficient for clearance measurement. The four counties, including Songjiang, will be launched immediately. They are instructed to make proper contacts when the clearance measurement team arrives and protect them at any time. County Magistrate Jin has instructed all district chiefs to comply.

Discussion on Dredging Changshan River 103

The Changshan River connects various ports such as Zhu Jing and Songyin in Jinshan County to the south. The river course is tortuous, with a bend every three li. The river is gradually silting up and cannot be navigated. The rice industry in the Xitan area of this city is greatly affected. The sale of agricultural products along the river is also inconvenient. Various sectors have been planning to expand the dredging, but it has not been held. Now, during the dredging of the city river, County Magistrate Jin invited Cai Zhongyu, chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, and Zhang Jiliang, the leader of the rice industry, to discuss dredging. The cost of dredging the river is approximately 6,000 yuan. The Xitan rice market has an annual business of approximately 300,000 dan. Assessing a dredging donation of two cents per dan will generate enough revenue in one year to cover the dredging costs. Both the rice industry and farmers will benefit. It is reported that Zhang Jiliang said that he will report back after convening a meeting of the Rice Industry Association.

Su-Mu Establishes Long-Distance Bus 104

The roadbed for the Su-Mu highway from Suzhou to Mudu was built three years ago. Now, Liu Fuqing and others have initiated and raised 50,000 yuan to establish the Su-Mu Long-Distance Bus Company, which has been approved by the Jiangsu Construction Department for filing. They are now engaged in soliciting shares and expect to be able to operate within approximately three months.
