Wang Xiangbao and others also opened the He Xing Chicken and Goose Shop and also obtained a short-term operating permit from the tax office. Therefore, Ju Xing believed that Director Jiang of the tax office was interfering with their business and negotiated with the office but to no avail. They photographed the evidence and, in addition to filing a lawsuit with the local court, demanding compensation for business losses, appealed to the Ministry of Finance. Citizens Wang Ligeng and others also submitted a petition to the Ministry of Finance, accusing Director Jiang of malfeasance and fraud, requesting his dismissal to warn officials.

Wuxi

Preparing for the Establishment of the Land Bureau 106

The director of the preparatory office of the County Land Bureau was previously concurrently held by the county magistrate to handle land affairs. Recently, the Provincial Land Bureau, in order to rectify the land throughout the province, specially appointed Fu Shengen to come to Wuxi to serve as the director of the preparatory office of the Land Bureau. It has been over a month since he took over. In order to understand the actual situation of the Qing Wen Tu Gen (clean document and chart root) work, Fu decided to go to the countryside on the 23rd of this month to conduct on-site investigations in order to clarify the situation. The current Tu Gen team's group headquarters is stationed in Tangtou Town in the sixth district, divided into three teams to separately measure the scenery and root points. The clearance measurement teams are stationed behind the Railway Hotel, also divided into two groups, the first group in Zhouxin Town and the second group in Nanqiao, to carry out clearance measurement work. It is also reported that five counties, including Zhenjiang, Jiading, Qingpu, Danyang, and Fengxian, have already established Land Bureaus to handle land tax registration. The remaining counties, including Wuxi, Wuxian, and Wujin, are still in preparation and are expected to be formally established and begin registration in about three months.

Arson Case Scheduled for Joint Hearing 107

The Xie Sheng Silk Shop in the city's Dashiqiao was suspiciously set on fire on the night of December 4th last year, spreading to several neighboring homes. Afterwards, Zhou Erkai, the chief prosecutor of the County Court, received a secret report that the shop was suspected of arson and successively arrested Fan Jingwen, the manager of the shop, and Su Jin Chu, the manager of the insurance company, for interrogation and detention. Fan was released on bail with a written guarantee of 4,000 yuan. Recently, Chief Zhou filed a public prosecution with the criminal court of the same court. Judge Liu has scheduled a hearing at 1:00 PM on the 24th of this month, summoning Su Jin Chu, who is in custody, as well as Fan Jingwen, Wang Zhenxin, Chen Huangshi, Chen Nianzu, Zhang Renshan, Wang Yunong, Wang Liangqing, and Liu Ruisheng to the court for questioning in order to verify and handle the case.

Jiading

Discussing the Establishment of a Joint Cooperative 108

On the 19th, the county government convened the Rural Improvement Committee. All agreed that rescuing the rural economy was a crucial and effective method. Based on the situation in the county, each township should form cotton production and sales cooperatives in groups, and the entire county should establish a joint association of cotton production and sales cooperatives to concentrate the talents and strength of the entire county. The Farmers Bank should provide economic assistance in order to avoid empty talk. The following resolutions were made: (1) Each county district will separately convene rural leaders to organize cotton production and sales cooperatives. (2) Before the establishment of the joint association, the county government will hire various members of the party department, district chiefs, education directors, managers of the Farmers Bank, cooperative instructors, and one enthusiastic social worker from each district to form a design committee to plan detailed implementation methods. (3) The action plan includes promoting the use of millions of Huamian cotton varieties to gradually eliminate local cotton varieties, improving cotton planting methods to develop production quantities, dividing cotton into grades to meet market needs, eliminating the malpractices of selling cotton in order to consolidate sales credit, jointly transporting and selling to increase the income of members, jointly utilizing various equipment such as cotton ginning plants, packing plants, and warehouses required for production and sales operations, jointly borrowing the necessary funds for production and sales, and hiring specialized personnel to provide technical guidance. (4) In addition to membership fees and shares, equipment will be financed by the Farmers Bank at 60%, and the Farmers Bank will provide two yuan per mu for green seedlings, and the Farmers Bank will be fully responsible for transportation, sales, and mortgage lending. (5) Concurrently operate the promotion and planting of special agricultural products such as peppermint, pyrethrum, and okra, as well as special industrial products such as yellow grass fabrics.

Zhenjiang

Peng Case Continues to Be Heard 109

Peng Guoyan, the former magistrate of Pi County, who was detained by the local court, was prosecuted by the procuratorate for embezzling land taxes and malfeasance and transferred to the criminal court. Judge Xia Weishang opened a hearing, but the case was not concluded due to its complexity. Peng hired a lawyer to defend himself and requested bail, but it was not approved. Judge Xia issued another summons yesterday for relevant witnesses in the case to continue the hearing. As a result, because the summoned witnesses waited until 4 o'clock and did not report, Peng Guoyan was ordered to be returned to detention, pending continued summons and verification.

Yangzhou

Yuanchang Money Shop Closes 110

The local money industry opened on the 20th, with a total of eight shops, including Yisheng. The Yuanchang Money Shop has officially closed. The opening prices were: small foreign coins 77.5 cents, copper coins 32 cents, foreign silver exchange 15 cents, and early Shanghai silver orders 5 cents.

Qingjiang

General Situation of Profits and Losses of Various Industries 111

According to a survey conducted in Huaiyin City at the end of the old lunar year, of the money shops, Xiangtai, Fukang, Qingsheng, Zhengtai, Desheng, and Fukang made a profit, with the highest interest rate being 5,000 yuan and the lowest being 1,000 yuan. However, Shengda and Dehou went bankrupt due to losses, and Yutai closed down due to sluggish business. The reason for this is that it is difficult to use money in Zhenjiang, and the China Communications and Shanghai banks in Pu hold remittance funds, which hinders the development of the industry. The silk and cloth industry suffered losses and sold goods at reduced prices due to the large number of goods imported last spring and the low prices in the summer. For example, Dingda had a total of 400,000 yuan on its books, but the result was only a surplus of 2,000 yuan. The rest can be imagined. Jinyuanfeng closed due to share splits. The rest also had more losses than profits. As for the Beijing and Guangdong grocery industries, they also had no success due to the bankruptcy of the rural economy and the sharp decline in sales. Among them, Dashengchang, Dayouheng, Hongchangyi, Yufengtai (groceries above) and Chaochang, Sifuzhai, and Hongtaichang (Guangdong goods above) had small profits. The rest were only able to maintain the facade.

County Magistrate Bao Inspects Zhen-Cheng Road 112

The Cheng-Wu section of the Zhen-Cheng Road has been built for nearly a year. The Construction Department believes that the roadbed is too low and needs to be raised again. Construction began on the 4th and is scheduled to be completed at the end of the month. In order to promote the early completion of the road, County Magistrate Bao made a special trip to the countryside on the morning of the 20th to inspect the road along the way, up to Xishiqiao in the sixth district, and returned to the city that night.

After the big settlement on the 13th, Xiaoshan industries rested for five days according to custom to settle the year's profits and losses. Zhou Deyi Rice Shop, Shengda Money Shop, and Meihao Foreign Goods Shop were reorganized. The rest also had more losses than profits.

Shanghai Municipal Council Standing Committee to Consider Increasing Chinese Councilors 119

Whether it Can Meet the Wishes of the Chinese People

According to the North China Daily News, the election period for the Shanghai Municipal Council is approaching, and the organization of the Council is currently a problem. It is reported that the Standing Committee of the Council will convene a meeting on Wednesday afternoon to consider this matter. The Chinese Ratepayers' Association recently sent a letter to the Municipal Council, requesting an increase in the number of Chinese councilors. The current number is five, and at least four more need to be added, for a total of nine. The number of foreign councilors is also currently nine. This movement began when there were three Chinese councilors, and after it was increased to five, it continued to develop, leading to this request. According to sources on the Chinese side, this request is not based on the amount of taxes paid by the Chinese but on the original request made five years ago when discussing the issue of Chinese councilors. An official from the Chinese Ratepayers' Association stated yesterday that even if the number is increased to nine, considering the tax figures, it is still far from the number that should be. Three years ago, foreigners accounted for 45% of the taxes collected in the International Settlement, with the rest coming from the Chinese. At that time, the ratio of foreign to Chinese councilors was 9 to 5. According to statistics, the taxes paid by the Chinese have now increased to 64% of the total, while foreigners account for only 36%. If allocated according to this ratio, there should be 16 Chinese councilors. However, they do not want to demand too much at present, and in this transitional era, they would be satisfied with an increase of four.

Expedient Measures for Capital Conversion to Yuan 122

Ministry of Industry Orders the Bureau of Social Affairs

Law on Conversion of Company Capital to Yuan

The Ministry of Industry of the National Government has instructed the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs to supervise the abolition of taels and the conversion to yuan. To facilitate merchants and the public, three expedient measures have been drafted for the conversion of company capital from taels to yuan, and the bureau is ordered to comply. The measures are copied as follows: (1) For the total amount of company shares, converting taels to yuan at a fixed rate of 0.715, with every 10,000 taels becoming 14,000 yuan, a report should be submitted to the competent authority for record-keeping, without the need to apply for alteration of registration. (2) For the amount of each share, converting at a fixed rate of 0.715, with every 10 taels becoming 14 yuan, a report should be submitted to the competent authority for record-keeping, without the need to apply for alteration of registration. (3) Reissuing shares or adding stamps or notations on the shares is at the company's discretion.

Shanghai Electric Construction Company's Management Rights Discussed to Be Transferred from London to Shanghai 124

Shareholders' Committee Issues Notice of Opposition

According to a Reuters dispatch from London on the 20th, the Shareholders' Committee of the Shanghai Electric Construction Company has issued a notice to all shareholders, requesting them to instruct their representatives attending the shareholders' meeting to oppose the proposal to transfer the company's management rights from London to Shanghai. The committee claims to represent more than 51,000 shares. The Shanghai Electric Construction Company has scheduled a shareholders' meeting for March 14th to consider the distribution of dividends and the adoption of new articles of association. The new articles stipulate: (1) The location of the company's unified management is transferred from London to Shanghai; (2) All company and board meetings will be held in Shanghai thereafter; (3) All directors will be persons residing outside the United Kingdom; (4) All current directors will resign; (5) Share registration will be handled in both China and London; (6) The chairman and a majority of the directors must be British; (7) Amend the qualifications and remuneration of directors; (8) Form a London committee and other related matters; (9) Appropriate £60,000 from the public reserve as capital, and distribute the 60,000 unissued shares, considered fully paid-up, to the shareholders in proportion to their existing shares; (10) Appropriate another £10,000 from the public reserve as capital to pay up the capital of the 10,000 unissued shares, and these shares will be donated to the directors to compensate for their loss of office.

Unified Method for Business Firms' Account Booking and Telegraphing, Submitted to the Ministry 125

Interest Paid by the Postal Savings Bank

To be Implemented from March 1st

In order to facilitate business firms in sending telegrams, the Ministry of Communications has specially formulated a method for guaranteeing account booking and telegraphing, and now instructs all subordinates to implement it from March 1st. The gist of the instruction is as follows:

Instruction from the Ministry of Communications 126

The Ministry of Communications instructs various Telegraph Administration Bureaus, Shanghai and Tianjin Telegraph Bureaus, and various Radio Stations, stating that the various bureaus and stations have no uniform method for handling the prepaid telegraph fees of business firms. Some responsible personnel, including those in charge of accounting, have even concealed prepaid telegraph fees of business firms without reporting them, or have privately misappropriated or embezzled interest. The Ministry has specially formulated a method for guaranteeing account booking and telegraphing for the convenience of merchants and the public and for ease of audit. It is hereby copied and issued for compliance and for instructing the various subordinate bureaus to comply. Hereafter, when the various bureaus and stations receive telegraph fee deposits from business firms, in addition to strictly complying with the provisions of the three articles of this method, they should list them in a monthly register and submit a list for verification. Furthermore, the telegraph fee auditors of the various bureaus and stations should also closely audit the aforementioned guarantee deposits at any time. If there is any unauthorized misappropriation or deduction of interest, it should be secretly reported for thorough investigation. This order is for instruction.

Account Booking Method 127

The original text of the newly formulated method for guaranteeing account booking and telegraphing is as follows: (1) For the convenience of sending telegrams, various business firms may request the telegraph bureau or radio station to send account booking telegrams in accordance with the provisions of this method. (2) Any business firm applying to send account booking telegrams should deposit a sum of money in cash with the bureau or station in advance, according to the estimated amount of telegraph fees for each month, as a guarantee deposit for telegraph fees (hereinafter referred to as guarantee deposit). The amount shall not be less than 100 yuan. (3) When the bureau or station receives the guarantee deposit paid by the business firm, it shall issue a receipt as proof. This guarantee deposit shall be deposited into a bank by the bureau or station in separate accounts and shall not be withdrawn except in the following three circumstances: A. When the business firm fails to pay telegraph fees owed, and the bureau or station withdraws the funds to offset them. B. When the business firm stops sending telegrams, and the bureau or station withdraws the funds for refund. C. When the business firm reduces the number of telegrams sent, and the bureau or station withdraws a portion of the guarantee deposit for refund. (4) The interest on the guarantee deposit shall be paid to the business firm by the bureau or station when the bank settles accounts every six months. (5) The bureau or station shall issue an account booking telegraph receipt book to the business firm that has paid the guarantee deposit. When sending telegrams, the telegrams shall be sent to the bureau or station by presenting this receipt book. (6) The telegrams sent by the business firm that has paid the guarantee deposit shall be recorded in an account by the bureau or station at any time, and a list of telegraph fees shall be prepared at the end of the month for settlement with the business firm. After receiving the list, the business firm shall pay the full amount within three days, and the bureau or station shall issue a receipt as proof. If the payment is overdue, the bureau or station shall immediately suspend the account booking telegraphing for that account and deduct the telegraph fees from its guarantee deposit, refunding any balance. (7) If the telegraph fees incurred by the business firm that has paid the guarantee deposit exceed the amount of the guarantee deposit during the month, the bureau or station shall notify the business firm to add to the guarantee deposit at any time. If the addition is not made within three days after notification, the bureau or station shall, in addition to suspending the account booking telegraphing for that account, deduct the telegraph fees from the guarantee deposit and recover any remaining amount. (8) If a business firm reduces the number of telegrams sent, it may request the bureau or station to refund a portion of the guarantee deposit. (9) The guarantee deposit specified in Article 2 of this method may be replaced by a guarantee letter from a bank designated by the bureau or station. (10) This method shall be implemented from March 1, 1934.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Actively Engaged in Combined Water and Land Transportation

Guangdong Combined Transportation 128

Guangdong Province needs a lot of oilseed meal and beans every year. After the Northeast was lost, it switched to purchasing Northwest goods from ports such as Haizhou to make up for the deficiency. However, transporting raw kernels from Haizhou to Shanghai and then to Guangdong requires the payment of about 30 cents in customs duties per dan. The Longhai Railway Bureau and the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company have agreed to expand the old Yao combined transportation route and add a direct old Yao-Guangdong route to carry raw kernels, beans, and other goods to Guangdong. Since water freight is exempt from customs duties and can avoid the export customs duties for transshipment, it is greatly welcomed by the Guangdong merchants. It has now been agreed to dispatch ships soon. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has specially chartered the Yongheng and Shou Kang ships to increase voyages to the old Yao and add new routes to Guangzhou.

Pinghan Signs Contract 129

There are many combined transportation goods on the Pinghan Railway, especially ginned cotton, tung oil, miscellaneous grains, and mineral sand. The Ministry of Railways has urged the Pinghan Railway Bureau, which has also negotiated with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to hand over the combined transportation goods to the company's Yangtze River ships for loading. All the detailed rules of combined transportation have also been agreed upon. It is planned to implement it on the first of next month. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has sent Zhou Fengtu, Director of Combined Transportation, to Wuhan to sign detailed rules of operation with the Pinghan Railway, and progress is smooth. Zhou left for Wuhan on the 17th and will be able to return to Shanghai soon to prepare for implementation.

Foreign Communities Telegraph International Postal Conference 130

Accelerate Mail Through Siberia

Postal Authorities Claim No Responsibility

According to the Shanghai Times, the Shanghai Foreign Communities Association telegraphed the International Postal Conference convened in Cairo this month because the mail from Europe to Shanghai via Siberia was received too late. The wording of the telegram was quite firm, not only expressing the hope that the efforts of the conference would speed up the mail via Siberia, but also requesting that China reduce the postage for foreign mail, which is now 60% to 250% higher than in other countries. In recent months, mail via Siberia has taken four weeks to reach Shanghai, or even more than four weeks, whereas in normal times it takes only about 16 days. According to the postal authorities in this city, this is because the central government does not recognize the puppet state of Manchukuo, so European mail via Siberia has to be rerouted via Vladivostok and then by navy. If there are no ships directly to Shanghai, it must first be sent to Japan and then transferred to Shanghai, which causes delays. The postal authorities cannot be held responsible for this situation and there is no way to remedy it.

The Ship Collision Handling Committee Held Its Eighth Meeting Yesterday 131

The Case of the Tongshang Steamer Colliding with a Coal Boat in Xiaguan

A Letter Was Sent to the Jiangning Court Requesting the Release of the Captain for Trial

The Ship Collision Dispute Handling Committee of the Shanghai Navigation Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications held its eighth meeting in the conference room of the bureau at 3:00 PM yesterday. More than ten committee members attended, chaired by Zhu Yaoting, to discuss the following cases:

Cases Discussed (1) The case of the Daxing Shipping Company's Hongxing steamer colliding with the Lin Lifeng junk at the Wusongkou. It was resolved that the Hongxing side pulled back and retreated to the right, which was not in violation of the port regulations or the location. Based on various circumstances, the fault should be borne by the tugboat. The compensation for damages should be handled in accordance with the provisions of Article 112 of the Maritime Law. (2) The case of the Tonghua Shipping Company's Tongshang steamer colliding with Liu Longpu's coal boat on the Jiangning section of the Yangtze River near Nanjing, drowning five crew members. The captain of the Tongshang steamer, Zhang Huihuang, is currently being detained in the Jiangning Local Court. How should this be handled to find a solution? It was resolved that a letter should be sent to the Jiangning Local Court in Nanjing requesting the release of Zhang Huihuang to come to the meeting for trial.

Request for Release of Captain The bureau sent a letter to the Jiangning Local Court in Nanjing yesterday, stating: (Omitted) To the Honorable President of the Court, Regarding the case of the Tonghua Shipping Company's Tongshang steamer colliding with Liu Longpu's coal boat on the Jiangning section of the Yangtze River near Nanjing, the two parties have reported to the bureau requesting that the dispute be submitted to the Ship Collision Dispute Handling Committee of this bureau for adjudication. This committee was established by order of the Ministry and specializes in handling ship collision cases. Its organization is similar to foreign maritime courts. Furthermore, the responsibility for compensation for damages from ship collisions should be borne by the ship in accordance with the provisions of Article 115 of the Maritime Law. Therefore, we request that Your Honorable Court first release the captain of the ship, Zhang Huihuang, to come to the meeting for trial in order to determine responsibility. We hope you will investigate accordingly.

Deadline for Land Value Tax Extended to the End of the Month 135

The collection of land value tax in areas 1 to 7 of the Shanghai South District and areas 1 and 2 of the Zhabei District began on December 21st of last year and ended on February 20th of this year. Ninety percent of the property owners have paid the tax, and tax payments are still enthusiastic. It is reported that the Finance Bureau, considering that this tax is in its initial stage and that the addresses of a few property owners were unclear when delivering the notices, causing delays in receipt due to inquiries by the delivery person, and in view of the crowded situation at the collection office in recent days, some were unable to complete the payment. The Municipal Government was specially requested to extend the deadline for land value tax to the end of February this year. All property owners who complete the land value tax payment within the extended deadline will be exempted from the annual interest surcharge as a gesture of sympathy. Once the deadline expires, the annual interest surcharge will be added according to the regulations, and collection may be pursued through summons and prosecution.

The Peril and Rescue of Weng Wenhao 140

His Injuries Have Significantly Decreased

Regarding Weng Wenhao's ordeal, initial reports from various newspapers stated that he had collided with a long-distance bus, and the details of his rescue were also unclear. Now, a relative of the Weng family who returned to Shanghai from Hangzhou yesterday provided a very detailed account of the incident, including information previously unknown to others. We are publishing the following as a supplement:

On the morning of the 16th of this month, Mr. Chen Bokui, who works at No. 2 Jiujiang Road in Shanghai, Mr. Chen Binggang, who works at the Lixing Foreign Firm on Beijing Road, and Mr. Yu Bingyong, each accompanied by their wives, a total of seven people, chartered a long-distance bus from Beijing to Hangzhou for sightseeing along the way. Near Tai Lake, they saw Mr. Weng sitting alone in a car, which passed them. Around 4 p.m., when Mr. Chen and his party arrived at the scene of the accident, they saw Mr. Weng's car crashed against the side of a bridge. The uninjured driver of his car was kneeling on the ground, shouting for help. Local villagers from Wukang were also shouting for help. At that time, a private car, identified as Beijing 751, which was traveling from Beijing to Hangzhou, happened to be parked nearby. Only one person was in the car. After Mr. Chen and his party got out of their bus, they saw that Mr. Weng and another driver were seriously injured and bleeding profusely. They urgently considered sending the two injured men to Hangzhou for medical treatment by their long-distance bus, but because the long-distance bus would be very bumpy and slow-moving, they feared that the two men would lose too much blood and their lives would be endangered. They discussed with the passenger of car 751, requesting that he give up his car so that the injured could be sent to Hangzhou immediately. Mr. Chen and his party would then invite the passenger to share the long-distance bus with them. Unexpectedly, the passenger completely ignored them and drove away quickly. Mr. Chen and his party, eager to help, immediately carried the two injured men onto the long-distance bus, intending to rush to Hangzhou. At that time, Mr. Weng was still conscious and asked his driver where they were. Upon learning that they were close to Wukang, he said, "Go to Wukang first," and instructed the driver to drive slowly to avoid bumps. When the bus arrived in Wukang, they were initially unfamiliar with the place and did not know where the hospital was. Later, Mr. Chen and his party managed to find the police chief of the local Public Security Bureau and asked him to quickly telegraph Hangzhou to send a doctor to Wukang. When Mr. Weng got out of the bus, a repairman who had boarded at the Moganshan Bus Station volunteered to carry him on his back to the Wukang County Hospital for emergency treatment. After receiving the news, the Hangzhou Guangji Hospital immediately dispatched a doctor to Wukang at 11 p.m. that night. At 5 a.m. the next morning, Mr. Weng was sent to Hangzhou by the city government's ambulance. Reports in Nanjing newspapers claiming that Guangji Hospital refused to send a doctor are unfounded. Mr. Weng's relatives, hearing that Mr. Chen and his party had acted righteously and that Mr. Weng had been rescued in time, intend to have his family express their gratitude. As for the worker who carried Mr. Weng to the hospital, efforts are currently underway to investigate his name and address and to find a way to reward him.

Mr. Weng's condition has now greatly improved. His temperature and pulse have returned to normal. He is now consuming milk and other beverages, and his appetite is good. According to the doctors' preliminary examination, his brain and eyes are not affected. However, due to excessive blood loss, he is still weak. He has been conscious in recent days. Because Mr. Weng is concerned about public affairs and eager to recover, he is eager to have the bandages removed as soon as possible. The doctors still instruct him to rest quietly. It is now known that Dr. Niu Huilin came to Shanghai on the evening of the 19th. After taking care of personal matters, he returned to Hangzhou the next morning to specialize in his medical treatment. Instructor Qian Changzhao is still staying in Hangzhou to take care of everything. His family has also arrived in Hangzhou.

Preparations for the Establishment of the Shanghai County Experimental Township 141

Shanghai County is planning to establish an autonomous experimental township in Dingshan, Fengxiang, and Zhushan of the fourth district of Pudong, with the goal of achieving sound organization and economic prosperity through the center of elementary school autonomy. The regulations and outline of the implementation plan have been drafted and prepared, and a founding ceremony was held at 2 p.m. the day before yesterday at the township office. County Magistrate Pan Zhongjia, Fourth District Chief Fu Dianying, Madam Niu Yongjian, Huang Meixian, and five or six hundred people from various institutions, organizations, and all walks of life attended. The meeting was chaired by Township Chief Qiao Qilin, and County Magistrate Pan and others delivered speeches. The ceremony concluded successfully, creating a grand scene for a while. The outline of the experimental township plan is now recorded as follows: (A) Regarding organization: Thoroughly investigate the actual situation of the entire township, establish a strict neighborhood organization, implement personnel registration, establish a mediation committee, formulate a township covenant, and vigorously carry out defense training. (B) Regarding education: Establish elementary school branches, establish women's civil schools, teach martial arts, hold lectures, improve entertainment, and reward diligent students. (C) Regarding the economy: Improve farming, promote animal husbandry and planting, organize cooperatives, dredge rivers, build roads, promote frugality, establish clinics, assist the helpless elderly and young, and dissuade opium and gambling. The projects outlined in this plan are to be completed within three years, and the order of priority will be determined at any time based on the actual situation, with the principle of relying on local self-raised funds to carry out the work.

Forty-nine Men and Women Given Free Boat Tickets

Arrived in Tianjin by the Dingsheng Wheel and Then Sent Onward

They arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday and jointly requested relief from the Xinwei Relief Association, represented by Duan Zhenfeng and Ge Liangyou. Considering that it was not a long-term solution for the refugees to be stranded in a foreign land, the association issued each person a "Refugee Free Boat Ticket," a total of 49 tickets, and dispatched staff to negotiate with Wang Shengyi Ticket Office to ensure proper arrangements. Last night, the association escorted the 49 men and women refugees onto the Yihe Company's Dingsheng Wheel to return to their hometowns. It is reported that the ship is scheduled to sail to Tianjin this morning (the 22nd), and they will then be sent back to their hometowns separately.

The Ministries of Finance and Communications Approve Measures for Collecting Customs Duties on Postal Parcels 145

The Ministry of Finance stipulates that goods traveling to and from the interior, passing through customs, are not taxed. However, merchants take advantage of this provision, often sending postal parcels from the interior to trading ports to post offices near the ports to avoid taxes. This kind of clever smuggling not only results in tax losses but also inevitably leads to other corrupt practices. The Ministry of Finance consulted with the Ministry of Communications to instruct post offices and the relevant Customs Superintendents to draft measures for inspecting and collecting postal parcel taxes. It is now learned that the measures have been jointly agreed upon by the Postal Administration and the Customs Superintendent and have been carefully reviewed by the Ministries of Finance and Communications. The revised measures for collecting customs duties on postal parcels traveling to and from the interior are as follows: (1) Postal parcels traveling to and from the interior that pass through two or more trading ports will be inspected and taxed by customs, except for those that are exempt from tax according to regulations. However, if the goods are transported on the same route and are not required to pay customs duties, then postal parcels will also not be taxed. If they only pass through one trading port, customs will generally exempt them from inspection and taxation. (2) Postal parcels sent by land or railway in the interior will be exempt from inspection and taxation if the places they pass through are not within the customs' taxation scope. (3) The opening, inspection, and resealing of postal parcels that are subject to inspection and taxation will be jointly handled by customs and the post office. (4) The tax amount for postal parcels that need to be taxed should be estimated by the customs of the last trading port. (5) The customs duties that should be collected on postal parcels will be collected by the post office at the post office of arrival, based on the tax amount estimated by the customs, and 10% of the total amount will be deducted as a handling fee for the post office for collecting the tax, and the remaining amount will be remitted to the customs. If there is a difference in the currency systems between the two places, the post office may collect the exchange premium from the taxpayer. (6) These measures will take effect after being approved by the relevant departments of customs and the post office, and the specific rules for implementation will be determined separately.

Re-exported Shoes Are Not Allowed to Be Exempt from Tax 148

If Shoe Merchants Are Not Satisfied

They May Appeal to Customs in Accordance with the Regulations

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce previously reported to the Shoe Industry Association that shoe materials are imported and taxed according to the regulations, and after they are made into shoes, they are re-exported and should not be taxed again. The Chamber of Commerce reported the situation to the Ministry of Finance, requesting that the tax on re-exported shoes be reduced or exempted. If this is not possible due to general regulations, the ad valorem tax should be changed to a specific tax to maintain sales, etc. The Ministry of Finance has now issued a reply, stating, "The submission has been noted. The styles of shoes manufactured in recent years are becoming more and more innovative, and the prices are also different. Customs inspection and assessment are based on the true market price, and it is not possible to enforce a uniform standard. The original letter from the Shoe Industry Association stated that the tax was 10 cents per pair last time, and this time it is necessary to pay 12 cents or 16 cents per pair. What kind of goods are these shoes? No samples have been submitted for detailed description, and it is impossible to verify. If the shoe merchants are not satisfied with the tax levied by customs, they should, in accordance with customs regulations, lodge a protest with the Customs Superintendent within the specified time, requesting that it be sent to the Tariff Classification and Valuation Review Committee for review and submitted for approval to provide relief. The request to reduce or exempt the tax on re-exported shoes, or to change to a specific tax, is difficult to approve. Please immediately notify the Shoe Industry Association of this reply."

General Rules for Long-Distance Telephone Operations Will Be Implemented from March 1st 149

And the Format of the Forms Will Be Revised and Distributed for Application

The Ministry of Communications yesterday issued an order to the heads of the telecommunications administration bureaus, telephone bureaus, and long-distance telephone management offices under its jurisdiction, stating, "The General Rules for Long-Distance Telephone Operations have been promulgated, and the various form formats used for long-distance telephones have been revised by the Ministry. The operating rules and various forms have been printed by the Ministry and transferred to the Storage and Transfer Office for distribution to the various administration bureaus for redistribution and use. Those that are filled out and sent to the various administration bureaus by the various operating offices and agencies should continue to use the old forms until the existing stock is used up before switching to the new forms. Please forward these instructions for compliance."

Unemployed Workers in the Southern Goods Industry Surround the Labor Union to Demand Relief 150

After Sending Representatives to Reply, They Dispersed

There are more than 400 large and small stores in the southern goods industry in this city. Historically, the three major festivals of each year have been the period for dismissing employees. Since 1929, after the Southern Goods Workers' Union submitted a request to the Social Affairs Bureau for mediation, it was agreed that February 28th of each year would be the period for dismissing employees. However, in recent years, the business of various stores has declined, and the old practice is still being used. Last year, more than 500 people were laid off one after another. The workers, due to the difficulty of making a living, have requested that the labor union find a way to settle them, but this has not yet been realized. Yesterday afternoon at 1 p.m., more than 60 unemployed workers in the industry went to the union on Fuyou Road, demanding that representatives be sent to negotiate with the trade association to arrange for their settlement and maintain their livelihoods. The union then sent staff member Yu Yaoqiu to meet with them. Yu Yaoqiu replied to the workers, saying that the union would, in accordance with the provisions of labor-management conditions, submit a negotiation to the trade association, requesting the organization of an unemployment referral office to implement settlement. As for the unemployed workers, they should first register with the union and wait quietly for a solution. The workers expressed their satisfaction and dispersed at around 4 p.m.

Authorities in Five Provinces and Cities Unify Traffic Management Regulations 151

Formulating Uniform Measures for Driver's Licenses

To Be Implemented from April 1st This Year

Since the highways of the five provinces and cities of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Beijing, and Shanghai have been gradually completed under the supervision of the competent authorities of each province and city, traffic within the five provinces and cities will inevitably become more and more convenient in the future. However, due to the failure to unify various management regulations in the past, there have been many inconveniences. Therefore, the competent authorities of the five provinces and cities have formulated unified measures for automobile driver's licenses in the five provinces and cities of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Beijing, and Shanghai, which will be implemented from April 1st. Anyone who holds a driver's license from this city on April 1st can exchange it for a new unified license from April 1st without additional fees. The unified measures for automobile driver's licenses in the five provinces and cities are recorded as follows:

Unified License Measures (1) Anyone driving a car within the five provinces and cities must hold a unified automobile driver's license issued by the Transportation Committees of the five provinces and cities of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Beijing, and Shanghai. (2) The unified license mentioned in the preceding article is valid in the five provinces and cities and is formulated by the Transportation Committees of the five provinces and cities and distributed to the various provinces and cities for application. (3) Anyone who has obtained a single driver's license from any of the five provinces and cities before the implementation of these measures shall, within three months after the promulgation of these measures, bring their original license to the issuing authority of the respective province or city to exchange it for a unified license without additional fees. (4) The unified license may be kept by the licensee permanently, except when it is subject to inspection or suspension for violations or must be temporarily deposited due to special regulations. (5) The unified measures for examining automobile drivers will be determined separately by this committee. Before the implementation of these measures, all examination methods for newly issued licenses in the various provinces and cities will remain the same. However, they should still be exchanged for unified licenses within three months. (6) After the implementation of the unified measures for examining automobile drivers, all provinces and cities must follow them uniformly. When necessary, the Transportation Committees of the five provinces and cities may send personnel to assist. (7) The unified license number should be prefixed with the characters for Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Beijing, and Shanghai for easy reference. (8) Unified licenses should be divided into the following two types, and the license fee for each type is eight yuan: (A) Professional driver's license; (B) Ordinary driver's license. Of the aforementioned license fee, three yuan should be submitted to the Transportation Committees of the five provinces and cities to be used for road traffic signs, signals, safety equipment, and safe driving incentives in each province and city, and the remainder should be retained by each province and city. (9) Learner's permits will be handled by each province and city themselves, but they may not be valid in other provinces and cities. (10) The original regulations for managing drivers and issuing driver's licenses in each province and city will continue to be valid, except for those that conflict with these measures, which should be handled in accordance with these measures. (11) Detailed rules for the implementation of these measures will be formulated separately. If there are any matters not covered, they may be amended at the standing committee of the Transportation Committees of the five provinces and cities. (12) These measures will be resolved by the standing committee of the Transportation Committees of the five provinces and cities and sent by letter from the National Economic Council to the governments of each province and city, with a date set for simultaneous promulgation and implementation.

Draft Examination Rules (1) Anyone driving a car within the five provinces and cities shall be examined in accordance with these rules. (2) Anyone driving a car must be examined by the competent authority of the province or city in which they reside. (3) Applicants, regardless of gender, must be at least seventeen years old, be able to read and write, have sound limbs, be sharp of hearing and sight, and not have any mental illness. (4) Those who meet the qualifications of the preceding article and wish to take the examination must register with the local competent authority and pay a registration fee of one yuan, including the photo fee. Whether or not they are accepted will not be refunded. For each re-examination, an additional handling fee of one yuan will be charged. (5) Driver's licenses are divided into the following two types, which are approved by the competent authority: 1. Professional driver's license; 2. Ordinary driver's license. (6) The examination date will be determined by the local competent authority. (7) The examination matters will be carried out by specialists appointed by the competent authorities of each province and city. The scope of the examination is divided into the following five types: 1. Physical examination; 2. Traffic regulations; 3. Mechanical knowledge; 4. Driving skills (divided into stake test and road test); 5. Geographical knowledge. The above items 1 and 4 must be implemented with an actual examination, while items 2, 3, and 5 may be conducted orally. (8) After the applicant passes the examination, the local competent authority will issue a unified driver's license for the five provinces and cities, with a license fee of eight yuan per license. (9) The type of car that the driver is able to drive must be indicated on the driver's license as follows: 1. Light car; 2. Freight car; 3. Public car; 4. Motorcycle. Those who apply in the order of items 1, 2, and 3 above will be charged a handling fee of one yuan for each additional type, in addition to the fee charged in Article 8 for the first time. However, those who pass the third item on the first application will be exempted from the first and second items. (10) If a driver's license is lost, a guarantee letter must be obtained and submitted to the original issuing authority for reissuance, and a reissuance fee of two yuan must be paid. (11) Driver's licenses must be inspected once a year by any competent authority in the five provinces and cities, and a handling fee of one yuan must be paid. (12) Driver's management regulations will be formulated separately. (13) If there are any matters not covered in these rules, they may be amended by the Transportation Committees of the five provinces and cities. (14) These rules will be passed by the standing committee of the Transportation Committees of the five provinces and cities and sent by the National Economic Council to the five provinces and cities, with a date set for simultaneous promulgation and implementation.

Japanese Merchants Argue Against Japanese and American Dumping 152

Saying It Is Impossible

According to the Japanese-language Mainichi Shimbun yesterday, recently, Chinese newspapers have repeatedly reported that Japan will dump surplus rice on the Chinese market. However, according to Japanese merchants, the propaganda in Chinese newspapers is unfounded. The reason is that the cost of importing Japanese rice into Shanghai is 12 or 13 yuan per 100 catties, including import duties, while the market price of Chinese rice in this city is around 5 yuan. In comparison, Japanese rice is definitely difficult to sell in China. Moreover, the Japanese parliament is currently holding a meeting to discuss rice countermeasures. However, it is inevitable that Japanese rice will be dumped abroad in the future, but this is still impossible due to transportation and tariff relations.

The Shareholders of the Hai Feng Flour Mill Appeal Against Xu Hecheng for Fraud and Embezzlement 155

The Verdict is Scheduled for Announcement Yesterday

The Hai Feng Flour Mill in Haizhou was established in the late Qing Dynasty, during the Guangxu era, by the late Zhang Jian (also known as Zhang Ji Zhi) of Nantong, Yu Shounian of Huizhou, and others, with a total capital of 300,000 yuan. Initially, it was managed by Xu Jiuxiang. After Xu's death in the fourth year of the Republic (1915), the position remained vacant. From the seventh year of the Republic (1918) onwards, Xu's younger brother, Xu Hecheng, took over as the executive manager. However, the mill's business gradually declined, and it became insolvent. Consequently, the board of directors decided to liquidate the mill. Shareholder Wang Xiaowu was appointed as the auditor. The entire mill's property was leased by Hecheng to Gong Ji from the seventh year of the Republic (1918) to continue operations. In the twelfth year (1923), Gong Ji terminated the lease, and it was then leased to Xin Ji. In August of the nineteenth year (1930), the mill's buildings and equipment were insured against fire with Shanghai Dingxin Insurance Company for 100,000 taels of silver. On September 14th of last year, the mill suddenly caught fire and burned down. After Xu Hecheng received the compensation, he did not consult with the shareholders and unilaterally deposited 115,000 yuan of the compensation into the Jiaotong Bank in this city, disposing of the remaining funds freely. This dissatisfied Wang Xiaowu. Wang argued that Xu's appointment as manager of Hai Feng was not approved by the shareholders and was self-appointed. Having seized the title of manager, he took advantage of his position to embezzle the mill's assets. Wang then filed a criminal self-accusation against Xu in the First Special District Court, requesting that he be punished for the crimes of fraud and embezzlement. The initial trial resulted in a defeat for the plaintiff, Wang Xiaowu. Wang, unwilling to accept the outcome, hired lawyer Zhan Jifeng to appeal to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, vehemently stating the errors in the original judgment and demanding redress. Yesterday afternoon, the Second Branch of the High Court, consisting of Judges Zhao, Jiang, and Zhou, convened a collegial panel for the hearing, with Judge Zhao as the presiding judge. The appellant's lawyer, Zhan Jifeng, presented the appeal, stating that the appellee had impersonated the manager of Hai Feng and signed two lease agreements with Gong Ji, which constituted fraudulent behavior. As for the embezzlement of assets, the appellant was initially unaware of it, and therefore could not file the lawsuit earlier, until receiving the compensation and auditing the accounts, the appellant discovered that the appellee embezzled the insurance compensation, and the Dingxin Company paid over 125,000 yuan, but only 115,000 yuan was deposited into the bank, and the money was easily accessible, which was a sign of embezzlement, and the appellee paid 8,500 yuan to the insurance company, although someone admitted to receiving the money, their name was not the person who the appellee said, so the appellant thought that the appellee made a substitution on the spot, and the original verdict finding the appellee innocent was inappropriate. The appellant requested that the law be enforced. Xu Hecheng, the appellee, stated that he held 5,000 yuan of shares in Hai Feng, and his brother Jiuxiang held 10,000 yuan. After his brother's death, the position of manager was the responsibility of the board of directors. He was elected as liquidator by the shareholders in the seventh year of the Republic. Due to the passage of time, all written evidence such as letters had been lost. Xu Hecheng then detailed the process of leasing the mill to Gong Ji and Xin Ji twice between the seventh and nineteenth years of the Republic to raise funds to repay previous debts, and the situation of negotiating compensation with the insurance company after the mill was burned down last year. He also presented an account book to prove that the 115,000 yuan of compensation remaining in the Jiaotong Bank had been reported, and there was no embezzlement. Lastly, the appellee's lawyer gave a defense, and the court ordered that the verdict be announced on the afternoon of the 27th of this month.

The price is 20 yuan per dose, 10 yuan per half dose, and 5 yuan per box. Mail orders from other cities do not require additional postage.

Japanese Yellow Croaker Dumping 158

Sold for Only Fifteen Yuan Per Dan

Compatriots Should Pay Special Attention

Central News Agency reports that nearly 100 dan of the first batch of imported Japanese fish arrived on the Japanese ship "Manyimaru" the day before yesterday. They are all fresh small yellow croakers, caught in the sea near the Ma'anshan Islands along the coast of Jiangsu and Zhejiang in China. Each dan is sold for only fifteen yuan, more than twice the previous price. According to a report, one fishing boat imported more than 4,000 dan of Japanese fish in 1932, worth more than 85,000 yuan. This is only in Shanghai, and other ports are not included. It is reported that Japanese fish merchants are now mixing fish caught in Japanese fishing grounds with fish caught in Chinese fishing grounds in Qingdao and selling them in various places. Various salted fish are also being mixed. Recently, they have been using rapid freezing methods to pack fish caught on the original ship into cardboard boxes and directly transport them to various parts of China for sale.

Rescue Nets Are Not as Safe as Jumping Sheets 159

Reply from the Shanghai South District Fire Association to Wu Huatai

The Shanghai South District Fire Association replied to lawyer Wu Huatai, stating that it received the letter and acknowledged its contents. The association appreciated his concern for local public welfare and the well-being of the people. The association agreed that rescue nets were indeed excellent, but after studying the pros and cons, it found them not very satisfactory. Because the net is made of rope, the knots will weaken over time. Once weight is applied, it will break. This is extremely dangerous. Therefore, canvas is used, called jumping sheets. Although there is a slight recoil when jumping down, it is much safer than rope nets. Last year, when the new municipal government building was completed, the association participated in a high-jump performance. Those who jumped from the fifth floor were caught with the canvas. Jumping sheets are necessary for fire departments for emergency rescue. The association hopes Wu will continue to provide advice.

Lawyer Ding Shimin Did Not Authorize Him to Act as His Agent

The Court Reportedly Arrested the Fake Lawyer Yesterday

Recently, a man named Ding Zhongfu impersonated a lawyer and defrauded people. At the end of last year, he impersonated lawyer Ding Shimin and dared to appear in the First Special District Court. Ding Shimin investigated the matter and found that Ding Zhongfu rented a house at No. 22 Yide Lane, Penglai Road. The authorities went to the address at dawn yesterday. Ding Zhongfu was still in bed. Reason for the Postponement of the Ji Case 162

Xu Yuying Requested a Temporary Suspension

Petitioned the Supreme Court for a Change of Venue

Ji Juemi, the manager of Hartung, was accused of seducing the young girl Xu Yuying. The first trial ruled Ji not guilty. The plaintiff was not satisfied and appealed to the Second Branch of the High Court. The trial was originally scheduled to begin the day before yesterday afternoon, but it was suddenly postponed. The reason for the postponement was that Xu Yuying submitted a request to the Second Branch of the High Court before the scheduled hearing, requesting a temporary suspension, stating that she had separately submitted a request to the Supreme Court to transfer jurisdiction of the case and instruct another court to hear it. The Second Branch of the High Court believes that the case cannot be tried before the Supreme Court makes a decision on this issue. Therefore, in addition to approving the postponement, it has now submitted a request to the Supreme Court for review.

The First Special Court Examines Clerks 163

Adopting a Mock Trial Method

Examinees Record in Court

The Shanghai First Special District Court held an examination for court clerks yesterday afternoon. The examiners were Liu Yugui, a judge of the Criminal Division of the court, Chief Prosecutor Xiang Zhexun, and Ms. Tang Weishu, the chief clerk of the Criminal Records Section. The examination site was the Sixth Civil Court on the third floor of the court. Most of the examinees were clerks from the court, but there were also many students from middle schools and above. In total, there were about thirty to forty men and women. The examination method was different from ordinary examinations. There were no questions or essays. Instead, a mock trial method was used. Therefore, the courtroom was used as the examination site, and there was no need for special arrangements. The three examiners sat on the bench in their original roles, but all were in plain clothes and not in uniform. The examinees sat in the center of the court, each with pens, ink, paper, and inkstones on their desks. The court bailiffs acted as the litigants, such as plaintiffs, defendants, and witnesses, all of whom were present. Judge Liu then simulated a lawsuit and began the trial. The witnesses were questioned one by one, and Secretary Tang took notes. Chief Prosecutor Xiang also rose to argue the charges after the testimony. The only task of the examinees was to record the testimony of the litigants and the instructions of the judge. It is said that the criterion for grading and passing in the future will be based on the accuracy of the records. Secretary Tang's records will be used as a model. This type of examination is new and practical. The court first adopted this method last month for the examination of translators, and this is the second time.

A Fallen Flagpole Causes a Family's Ruin 165

Chen Ronggui's Wife Followed Him to the Grave

Leaving Behind Elderly Parents and Young Children

丨Old Jiatai Managerial Department Fined 500 Yuan丨

Chen Ronggui, a 38-year-old Suzhou man residing at No. 126 Jiuxiaochang in the city and working as a writer at Mee-Yeh Foreign Firm at No. 16 Guangdong Road, was heading home from work at around 5 PM on May 12th of last year when a flagpole falling from the roof of the Old Jiatai Tea Shop's back entrance at No. 6 Dazimingzhong, Dong Sheng Pawn Street, which is Old North Gate Main Street, struck him on the head and injured him. He later died of his injuries, leaving behind an elderly mother, Chen Zhang, in her sixties and blind, a widow, Chen Huang, and five children, as well as a virgin sister. Chen was the sole breadwinner. Since Chen's death, the family was in poverty. His relatives negotiated with Old Jiatai Tea Shop for compensation to support the family. The shop denied any negligence. The family retained a lawyer and filed a complaint with the Second Special District Court, accusing Old Jiatai Tea Shop owner Ye Jishan and manager Pan Jucai of causing death by negligence, requesting a trial according to the law, and seeking 50,000 yuan in damages. During the trial, the widow Chen Huang became ill due to grief and worry. By August, she also died, leaving behind her children and following her husband to the grave. Chen's mother, Chen Zhang, retained a lawyer and continued the lawsuit. The trial resulted in a verdict of not guilty for the defendant. The civil claim was dismissed. The plaintiff appealed to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. Following trials, investigations, and deliberations, the court issued a verdict the other day. The verdict stated that the original judgment regarding Pan Jucai was revoked. Pan Jucai was found guilty of causing death by negligence and was fined 500 yuan. If the fine is commuted to imprisonment, it will be calculated at three yuan per day. The rest of the appeal was rejected.

Wusong Party and Government Agencies Mediate Rent Disputes 168

Substantial Results Achieved

The buildings of Renchanghe Company on Wusong Waima Road were destroyed in the January 28th Incident. The new buildings have only recently been completed. The monthly rent for each building was set at 20.6 yuan. The tenants complained that the company's rent was 60% higher than before the war (8.3 yuan per month) and they were unable to afford it. They requested a reduction, which led to disputes with the residents. The Party, government, police, and business agencies mediated, but were unable to resolve the issue. In the second meeting the other day, Municipal Committee Member Tang Chengzong, Wang Chenge of the Eighth District Party Department, Yan Songbin, representative of the Chamber of Commerce, Gong Xikui, head of the Seventh District of the Public Security Bureau, Zhao Weixuan, representative of Renchanghe, and Dong Shangquan, representative of the Resident's Association, attended. Tang Chengzong chaired and Cao Qiweng recorded. After the chairman announced the purpose of the meeting, Zhao Weixuan, representative of Renchanghe, and Dong Shangquan, representative of the Resident's Association, successively stated their reasons. After discussion by the representatives of the four agencies, the resolutions were as follows: (1) Priority in leasing: (A) Fuchang Hotel Yang Juxing has agreed to move out. Renchanghe will subsidize Yang Juxing's renovation fee of 40 yuan and restore the original form when the lease is returned. (B) Xie Xingshun wants to rent a room. Pay half of the rent arrears, and pay the rest after renting a house to the south. The house behind the alley (No. 10) will be rented to Xie with Shun after the company asks the police to move out. (C) Dinglong rent house Shun Wenjie has reached an agreement with the new tenant, how to come forward to rent, directly contact the two parties. (D) Song Xinfang voluntarily waives the right to rent the house. (E) The old tenants who rent new houses must pay off all old debts. (2) Roof transfer issue: (A) Renchanghe follows the municipal government's rental rules, and the roof transfer is calculated at 60 yuan for three months. The payment of 65 yuan by each tenant will be deducted from the rent first. (B) The new house will be rented from March 1st. At the end of the meeting, the rent reduction issue had not been resolved, but the rest was settled.

1,537 People Arrested

The Police Department report for January states that 1,262 cases were reported during the month, an increase of 24 cases compared to the previous month and a decrease of 190 cases compared to the same month last year. 1,537 people were arrested. 114 people were arrested for old cases and 76 people were arrested on behalf of other government agencies.

Major Crimes 172

There were three attempted murder cases, two reported kidnapping cases (one of which was found to be inaccurate), one case of manslaughter, and five cases of armed robbery, an increase of 17 compared to the previous month and a decrease of 35 compared to the same month last year. 15 people were arrested for communist cases in January. 13 were handed over to Chinese authorities, one was released, and one was detained for questioning. 1,500 copies of communist literature were seized, including 35 types. The Zhenxing Woolen Mill in Xujiahui Road in this city specializes in imitating serge, woolen cloth, and Shuanglong brand woolen yarn with domestic raw materials. The products are of excellent quality and low price. Since its sales, it has been famous all over the country. The general manager of the factory, Gu Xiyuan, sees that foreign goods are flooding the market, money is flowing out, and the rural economy of our country is bankrupt and all industries are declining. If we do not seek to revive the rural economy, promoting domestic goods is equal to singing a high-sounding tune. Therefore, in addition to working hard in the textile industry, Mr. Gu also raised funds in Nanxiang Town last year to organize the Zhenxing Rural Side Industry Association, purchasing looms, releasing yarn for weaving cloth. Since its opening, it has achieved remarkable results. It is reported that the association is now planning to add dozens of looms to expand its scope, so as to avoid the regret of the villagers. It is hoped that those who are enthusiastic about reviving the rural industry will quickly start planning.

Publication of Books Should Adopt the New System of Weights and Measures 178

Yesterday, the Ministry of Interior issued a circular to the Municipal Government

Instructing publishing and distributing houses to comply

Yesterday, the Ministry of Interior issued a circular to the Municipal Government stating: "Regarding the approval of Industrial Ministry’s document number 8781, it opens with the National Bureau of Weights and Measures reporting: 'Upon investigation, the new system of weights and measures has been gradually and widely implemented. Currently, there are numerous books published nationwide, yet many still use the old system or the systems of Britain, America, and Japan. If this is not strictly rectified, it will greatly hinder future standardization. It is proposed that Your Ministry forward a circular to the Ministry of Interior to instruct the entire country that, hereafter, when reviewing new publications according to the Publication Law or Copyright Law, if it is discovered that they employ units and names not in accordance with Articles 4 and 5 of the Weights and Measures Law, and Articles 52 and 53 of its revised implementation rules, they should be returned with instructions for correction. However, if necessary, an annotation of the equivalent value in other systems may be attached. As for books that have already been reviewed and registered, please also instruct that they be corrected upon reprinting. For those already printed, a simple conversion table and a list of corrections should be attached to each copy to assist in promotion and demonstrate permanent standards. This matter concerns the transmission of culture. Is this appropriate? We hereby respectfully submit this for your review and adherence, etc.' In light of this, it is found that published books are the pioneers of culture. If the weights and measures used in books do not comply with the current system but continue to use the old system or foreign systems, it not only violates laws and regulations but also hinders promotion. The Bureau’s requests are feasible. Please investigate, verify, and report back for handling, etc.' Approved. In addition to separate distribution and replies, we hereby issue a circular requesting you to examine and instruct the publishing and distribution establishments within your jurisdiction to comply. We hope to receive a reply."

Hu Xiyuan, Economic Committee Member of the Women's National Goods Year, Resigns as Convener 179

Due to the expansion of Apple's business, he is often away from Shanghai

He will remain an Economic Committee member after resigning as Convener

Since its establishment, the Women's National Goods Year Movement Committee has been divided into an Economic Committee and a Design Committee. Each committee member has made great efforts to promote national goods. Recently, Hu Xiyuan, General Manager of the Apple Electric Factory, due to the expansion of factory operations, with branches and distribution centers being established in major commercial ports, and his need to frequently inspect business in other locations, believes he lacks the time to serve as the convener of the Women's National Goods Movement Economic Committee, fearing he would be holding a nominal title, hindering the national goods movement. Yesterday, he sent a letter to the Women's National Goods Association resigning from his previous position. The original letter is excerpted below: "To the esteemed Association, since the establishment of the Association, Xiyuan, with his limited talents, has been following the gentlemen who are enthusiastic about national goods, working in various ways, hoping to contribute a bit of his foolishness. At the previous meeting, the Economic Committee and the Design Committee were created. Xiyuan was mistakenly trusted and promoted as the convener of the Economic Committee. As this concerns the national goods movement, he dared not neglect his duties. However, due to the recent outward expansion of his personal business, he spends more time in other locations. Economics is the driving force of everything. If the convener is holding a nominal title, he fears it would hinder the future of the national goods movement. Therefore, Xiyuan is willing to remain as a member of the Economic Committee, and requests that the Assembly elect another person for the convener position to avoid delaying important matters, etc."

Rickshaw Pullers' Union Seeks Justice for Deceased Rickshaw Puller Ji Xueqing 180

Hiring Two Lawyers to Demand Punishment of the Culprit and Compensation

The preparatory office of the rickshaw pullers' union, yesterday at 3:00 PM, convened a meeting during which the family of the deceased Ji Xueqing reported that the deceased, at approximately 10:00 AM on February 12th, pulling rickshaw number 6650, registered under British jurisdiction, was traveling on Nanjing Road from west to east. At the entrance of Sanyang Southern Goods Store, he obeyed the rules of the concession, and stopped upon seeing a red light. Unexpectedly, the driver of public bus number 15071, Han Chunlin, traveling from east to west, disregarded the Public Works Department’s order to stop at a red light, driving like a shooting star, swerved across the road from the south side to the north side, completely destroying rickshaw number 6650 and fatally injuring the rickshaw puller Ji Xueqing, who was torn apart. The union was requested to uphold justice and provide assistance, to seek justice, etc. The committee members discussed the matter and determined that the bus driver Han Chunlin lacked driving experience, recklessly caused a fatal accident, was extremely negligent, not only damaged the rickshaw business but also treated the lives of rickshaw pullers as a game. The bus company should be held responsible for negligence in hiring. As a result, committee member Chen Guoliang was publicly selected to hire lawyers Wu Kaisheng and Chen Wenxiang as representatives of the family, demanding three points according to law: (1) Ji Xueqing was tragically killed, with an estimated loss of one yuan per day from the age of twenty to fifty, amounting to a minimum compensation of 10,000 yuan, in addition to expenses for clothing, coffin, and the damaged rickshaw; (2) demand that the bus company strictly prohibit inexperienced people from driving, guaranteeing that this type of disaster will not happen again in the future; (3) severely punish the perpetrator Han Chunlin according to law, to redress the injustice.

The Jiahe Steamer Runs Aground in Zhenjiang 185

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiahe steamer, conscripted by the military last month along with the Taishun, Guangli, Xinming, and Wuyang, to transport the 19th Route Army to Nanjing and then to Henan for reorganization, was carrying troops to Nanjing and then to Fuzhou when it ran aground in Zhenjiang. The details are as follows:

Aground Mid-Voyage: The Jiahe steamer transported troops from Fujian to Nanjing, unloaded them, and then set sail for Fuzhou with military supplies. It then loaded Fujianese troops to transport them to Pukou. Unexpectedly, on the afternoon of the 20th, the Jiahe steamer ran aground on a shoal opposite Shierxu upstream from Zhenjiang, due to the error of the river pilot. The ship was deeply mired, and it was impossible to escape the predicament.

Military Terminates Charter: After the steamer ran aground, the shipowner immediately telegraphed for help to Nanjing and Shanghai. The Naval Transportation Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs, concerned that there were military supplies on board, urgently dispatched a ship to the grounding site to transfer the contents of the Jiahe, as well as the soldiers, to another steamer for transportation to Fuzhou. The Naval Transportation Department, under pressure to transport cargo, could not wait long and telegraphed the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company yesterday, terminating the charter of the Jiahe.

Company Rescue Efforts: Yesterday, upon receiving the report, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's shipping department discussed rescue plans. In addition to telegraphing the Zhenjiang branch to attempt to dispatch a ship to tow the Jiahe, they also sent a letter to each of the Zhaotai Insurance Companies regarding the cause of the Jiahe steamer's grounding and the rescue plan. They currently plan to make a decision after consulting Guangli upon its return to Shanghai.

Review of the Three Kidnappers in the Zhang Changfu Case After Serving Their Sentences 186

Zhang Changfu, a deceased Ningbo native who was a comprador for the French business Pathé Records, located at 120 Route Lafayette in the French Concession, was kidnapped by bandits in the French Concession on November 12, 1928, and a large ransom was demanded. After being held for a week, his family paid the ransom. The French police subsequently arrested twelve kidnappers, including Xu Liugen, Zhu Ada, Zhang Shilin, He Yingshan, and Li Shuilin, who were sent to the former French Court for trial. The defendants confessed to the kidnapping and were sentenced to five years imprisonment each, after which they were to be handed over to the mainland authorities for further proceedings (however, many of the defendants, such as Xu Liugen, died in custody of illness; only Zhang Shilin (from Wuxi), He Yingshan (from Sichuan), and Li Shuilin (from Ningbo) survived). Now, with their five-year terms completed, the Second Special District Prison transferred Zhang, He, and Li to the Second Special Court for review and notified the police. Yesterday, Judge Qiu Huan Ying questioned them in the Criminal Court. First, Police Lawyer Yao Zhaodi presented the case. Zhang, He, and Li all testified that they were not involved in the kidnapping, had been wrongly detained, and had been imprisoned for five years, requesting vindication. Subsequently, Detective Zhang Daorong, who handled the case, reported on the investigation and arrest of the defendants after the kidnapping occurred. The court ordered the case to be postponed until March 2nd and instructed the detective to produce a written report for further interrogation. The defendants were returned to custody.

Tram in Songhu Kills an Old Woman 189

Yesterday at 2:40 PM, a steam train from Fort Wusong to Shanghai, was traveling near Zhanghuabang, when an old woman was walking beside the railroad tracks. Son-in-Law Beats His Mother-in-Law to the Point of Incontinence 190

Truly, a Case of Extreme Cruelty

The family of the old lady, surnamed Wang, who resides in Gaochang Lane, is originally from Ningbo. She is 51 years old and has three daughters. Her second daughter, Huiqin, is 18 years old this year. On January 1st of the current year, arranged by matchmaker Peng Chen, she was married to Quanlun, son of Zhuang Xiuru (who works as an accountant at Yuxinxiang Foreign Goods Store in Dapuqiao). Quanlun works at the Xiangxing Knitting Factory on Daji Road. Unexpectedly, just three days after the wedding, Huiqin was slapped and beaten by her husband. Unable to endure the abuse, Huiqin returned to her mother's home and wept to her mother. Old Lady Wang was about to go to reason with him when Zhuang Quanlun accused Old Lady Wang of fraud and reported her to the district police station. The police summoned them to the station and, upon hearing the matter, deemed it a minor issue and a family matter. The police advised both parties not to take extreme measures and to reconcile. The police advised Zhuang Quanlun to take his wife back and reconcile. The incident subsided. However, just a few days later, Huiqin returned home twice more, weeping, saying that all her jewelry had been taken by her husband and that she had been beaten. Old Lady Wang, out of love for her daughter, comforted her and let her stay at home for the time being. She planned to send her back to her husband's home after reconciliation. Unexpectedly, at around 8 PM the night before, Old Lady Wang was beaten by Zhuang Quanlun and others, even to the point of extreme incontinence and being covered in excrement. She was severely injured and was rushed to Nanyang Hospital for treatment by her family. Yesterday afternoon, Old Lady Wang was transported by the hospital's ambulance to the District Court, requesting an examination.

Fire at Changhe Pharmaceutical Store on Li Xian Gua Street 191

Extending to Two Neighboring Businesses

Losses Exceed 200,000

Changhe Pharmaceutical Store, located at No. 67 Li Xian Gua Street outside Xiaodongmen in Nanshi, has been in operation for over a decade. The manager, Kong Xiangui, is adept at business, and the store's business is usually quite prosperous. Unexpectedly, yesterday at around 2 AM, a fire broke out in the store's third storage building, for unknown reasons. In an instant, flames soared and burst through the roof. When the fire brigade heard the alarm, they immediately rang the bell. Soon, fire trucks from various fire brigades arrived on the scene to connect to water and fight the fire. By this time, the fire had spread to the rear of the neighboring businesses, Yuanchang (No. 63) and Jiukang (No. 71), both ginseng and bird's nest stores. Furthermore, Changhe's stock of medicinal materials was large and highly flammable. For a time, the fire illuminated the sky, and thick smoke filled the air, making it impossible to control. With the firefighters' utmost efforts, the fire was extinguished at around 4 AM. In the blaze, all fifteen of the store's three-bay, three-story buildings were completely destroyed. The rear buildings of Yuanchang Ginseng and Bird's Nest Store (three rooms) and Jiukang Ginseng and Bird's Nest Store (two rooms) were also affected and burned down. The estimated losses are over 200,000 yuan. When the fire broke out, the officer in charge of the district, Guo Jifen, dispatched a large number of police officers to maintain order. He took Ningbo native Ying Yuru, a store employee, back to the district, and District Chief Zhou conducted a preliminary interrogation before ordering him to be transferred to the Shanghai Public Security Bureau for further investigation. It is said that the store has fire insurance worth over 100,000 yuan.
