Free Talk

Eccentric 256

— Liaoran

Since science has become enlightened, it has made the spirit of mankind much younger. In science, the old is generally not good, the new is good. For example, using a hot iron to crimp hair to make it fluffy is no longer very fashionable, and it is far inferior to the permanent fluffiness of electric perms. This is certainly the good of the new.

However, "later generations will view today as today views the past." To make many old stubborns flutter. Are the noses of today's youth so high? Don't rush, in twenty years they will be about the same as us. We were also the new party twenty years ago. Wait until they have also suffered blows and see that their arrogance is completely gone, then we can compare who is stubborn!

The conflict lies in the belief that the new is all good or bad, and the old is all bad or good. If the standard is fixed like this, many problems will arise. There is no name for it, so it is named eccentric disease.

Youths wearing Western suits and smoking pipes make the older generation in long robes and mandarin jackets sigh, thinking it is extremely eccentric. When the youth also play with antiques and read thread-bound books, it makes them even more surprised. Have they also taken our path? It turns out that foreigners also read Confucius. And our new things also cover everything. The new is always good.

However, new and old, good and bad are all relative terms. So where is the standard for the new? The hats of Paris women have never been the same, and everyone twists into a different shape, always a little newer than others. However, it is said that in Chinese literature, the literary theories of Lunacharsky and others are not considered new, only Gorky will do; but Gorky has also become an old writer and will not be able to update to where, and it is still not good. Then it still depends on the length of the new writer's hair or the size of his black bow tie.

So it is very difficult to make people feel good these days. Fewer people are playing with national quintessence and Sinology because they gradually feel that although Taijiquan is good, it cannot resist the foreign devils' whips or guns. This is very frustrating, and there is no way to do it. Pilkad is newly thinking of going to heaven, while someone in Shanghai wants to sit on a pillar for sixty days. This should also be counted as a new world record. But what exactly is good?

It is said: It is not difficult to see. In short, come up with something eccentric. For example, when writing an article, cite a large passage from ancient history to create a new type of writing; in painting, mix Western and Chinese techniques together. Westerners look at it as Eastern painting, and Easterners look at it as Western painting. It is best to mix Chinese and English when speaking; when dressing, wear a shirt and trousers inside, then wear leather shoes and overshoes, then add a long robe, then add a coat, forming a style that is neither Chinese nor Western, so that it is neither new nor old and can be used everywhere.

One more thing to pay attention to is that in addition to being eccentric, add a little unintelligible quality to make people feel eternally vague, which can be considered newer and more fashionable.

Pseudo-Manchukuo Students Studying in Japan 257

— Yu Shixia

A friend who just returned from Japan talked about the recent situation of students studying in Japan, which is truly both infuriating and hilarious. Once, a classmate was taken to the police station by plainclothes detectives because of some suspicion. They asked him where he was from? He said: "Republic of China." He was slapped twice. They asked again, and he said: "Liaoning Province." He was slapped twice again. They asked again, and he said: "Fengtian." He was still slapped twice. He thought he didn't want to suffer this immediate loss anymore, so when he was interrogated again, he had to answer: "Manchukuo." Unexpectedly, he was slapped twice again. He really didn't know how to answer. Finally, they asked him, and he said: "Slave of a conquered nation." The Japanese police couldn't help but grin, but he was filled with sadness and burst into tears.

When school opened last autumn, the Industrial University held entrance exams, and all sixteen Chinese students who took the written exam were admitted. Unexpectedly, during the oral exam, only fifteen were admitted. The student who failed the exam went to question the school authorities. The authorities asked him where he was from? He said: "Republic of China." They asked him what province he was from? He said: "Liaoning Province." They asked him, "Does Liaoning still belong to China?" He was panicked and didn't know how to answer, but in order to enter the school, he had to answer against his will: "Manchukuo." The school authorities nodded and smiled and admitted him.

After the September 18th Incident, many Chinese students studying in Japan returned home. Only seven or eight hundred remained. Now it has increased to two thousand, with students from the Northeast provinces accounting for about one-sixth, and the rest being mostly students from the provinces of Guangdong, Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Sichuan, and Hunan.

Originally, there was a Republic of China Student Association in Tokyo, but recently this organization has disappeared invisibly. Should students from the northeastern provinces still call themselves Republic of China students or so-called "Manchukuo" students? This is of course one of the important reasons why the student association could not be organized, not to mention the different ideological factions!

Students who call themselves so-called "Manchukuo" students receive more government funding, at least 100 yuan or more. The Japanese seem to be deliberately trying to win them over, so they are treated relatively well. Some of them also see themselves as superior to Republic of China students, which is truly absurd.

The above records the words of a friend studying in Japan.

Evening 258

— Ms. Cao Ming

That winter, eleven silk factories in our village closed down one after another. When my work was suddenly stopped, I ran to the city without looking back to find work, staying in the home of a young paternal cousin who lived off his father's inheritance. His house, though not very large, had a living room, three rooms, and a spacious courtyard. Besides his elderly mother, there was also a nanny. However, a group of friends who were very compatible with him often gathered there, making noise all night long.

I wanted to escape the eyes of the city people from my country girl's habits, so I often preferred to run to the kitchen to help the nanny cook.

After dinner, Uncle Ba, his friends, and my great-aunt, who held her water pipe all day and refused to let go, were sitting in the living room as usual. After washing my feet in the kitchen, I leaned against the door frame, gazing sadly at the sky, dressed in dim clothes, with sparse stars inlaid all over. In the southern corner, the light blue cold clouds depressingly covered my declining hometown, Shunde. The bright lights in the living room, accompanied by the men's wolf-like conversations, shone through the corridor. Outside the street, the monotonous and brittle sounds of the huqin and pipa vibrated, passing behind our house, gradually being swept away by the cold wind.

My great-aunt, acting like the madness of young people, waved her hand at me almost breathlessly and said, "Lingnu, quickly call Blind Sister in..."

I first put the child in a scarf, shrugged my shoulders, and rushed out of the alley like a fire ship breaking through the waves of cold air. My discontinuous shouts, blocked by darkness, disappeared into the bleak, proud sound of the zither. A withered old nanny, dragging two blind girls, one thin and long, one fat, followed me like a few sheep. The moon, just peeking out with a sorrowful face, calmly and dimly illuminated their careful steps, their shoe soles never leaving the ground.

The old nanny took off their half-new cloaks, and their wind-blown, about-to-tear, purple-red muscles quickly trembled, preparing to absorb the indoor warmth. After they drank the hot tea I poured for them, they mechanically joked with the men in a vulgar tone. When the girls rapidly began to sing, the men pricked up their ears and stared, as if trying to search for something, fixing their gaze on them.

"Where is the toilet?" The song stopped, the old nanny quietly walked to my side, tugged at my sleeve, and asked in a low voice, then pointed to the thin and long one. I took the blind girl to my small room and sat by the bed, watching her gloomy face under the dim yellow light, which contradictorily held a smile with unshed tears.

"Have you been unable to see since you were a child?" I asked her.

"Yes, I have," she said coldly.

"I heard people say that for you singers, smiling is very important," I said, as if dissatisfied with her smile. She responded indifferently with only a nasal sound. I became even more unhappy and added:

"I don't think you've ever cried, have you?"

"To me, isn't it the same!" she said roughly, but then laughed as if to make light of herself, "Really, what's the difference between crying and laughing? I can't see."

"When I was in the countryside, I often heard stories about your life and your godmother..." The chaotic laughter in the living room flashed into the room from time to time, and I continued, looking at her rouge-dyed face, "Do you often feel bad in your heart? Do you hate your godmother?" She frowned but didn't answer. "Actually, people like us who beg others our whole lives are just like crabs in a pot of hot water," I said, and then fell into contemplation.

"People are creatures that eat their own kind, that's how I feel." Her sudden loud voice startled me, and I quickly raised my head. "As long as he grabs that kind of thing. Yes, whoever it is, as long as they grab those filthy things, they can jump up and eat people..." Finally, she ended her words with laughter, "Besides, I can't see anything."

Her face was so serious and gloomy that I stood beside her, feeling like I was tied to the thorny branches of a wild rose.

"Really, I'm often afraid... I don't know what's around me..." she said in a timid voice as she walked through the corridor.

After ten o'clock, the old nanny carefully checked the six dimes she had earned, and the three of them walked out of the gate like a freighter being towed by a tugboat, a string of wriggling shadows slowly dissolving into the black sea.

Interesting Metaphors 259

— Shu

(10)(4)

He Qiaoyuan wrote to Zhuang Yingshu, saying: "When you write poetry, do you intend to have it read to people while you are still alive? Or leave it for people to read after your death? If you are alive and Zhuang Yingshu is by your side, you can say: My poetry is like this and like that. But if you are dead and leave it for people to read, then you must make your meaning understood by hundreds of generations to come, so that readers can understand it for themselves. You can no longer say from the side, 'Is my poetry like this?'" Many writers often like to seek strangeness and interest in their poetry and prose, intentionally writing in a bizarre way, making it incomprehensible, and instead praising themselves for a kind of originality, even going so far as to explain themselves with thousands of words. If this is true, the interesting metaphor of before and after death, saying the ultimate truth that one wants people to understand, can be said to be prescribing the right medicine for the right disease, leaving them speechless. This is why Li Ning refused the futurist sculptor to create a statue for Karl.

(10)(5)

There are quite a few articles discussing "puppets," and recently, seeing Zhou Qi's letter to He Shengzhai, it was discussed again. He said: "When I was young, I saw puppet shows, two feet long, with many strings, manipulated by others. Recently, they have become only a few inches long, pushed with wooden boards, completely like those who think they are using their own intelligence. Alas! Puppets are also gradually becoming smaller, let alone people. Puppets also do not rely on human strings but want to use their own intelligence. How fearsome and sad!" Now, two hundred years later, their sadness is even greater. Because with puppets, in those days, you knew it at a glance. But now it's not the same. Those that are skillfully made not only make you unaware but even the puppet itself pretends to be serious and explains itself to people. This is how sycophantic literature and comprador literature are produced. Some people say that Chinese history is a history of slavery. In fact, it is also a history of puppets. I wonder if anyone agrees with my humble opinion?

(10)(6)

"Long rain without clearing, everyone dragging mud and water; only when the clouds open and the sun appears, and the right eye is wide open, can one do somersaults in the void. Meeting different peaks, one will naturally create their own writing. Please, Your Excellency, complete the previous words." This is Huang Duanbo's letter to Huang Zi'an. The article is written in a free and elegant style, and the two interesting metaphors, "dragging mud" and "somersaults," are used extremely vividly.

(10)(7)

Liu Dasheng discussed with Yu Jisheng about being an official, saying: "The world considers being an official the most serious matter, and acting in a play the most illusory. But I am very foolish, and every time I see singing, crying, laughing, scolding, jokes, and ad-libs on stage, I am sure that they are real. The reality is not in the ancient people being portrayed, but in the actors portraying the ancient people, each with parents, wives, and children, each having to support their families, each using crying, laughing, and jokes to support their parents and support their wives and children. These actors are the real ancient people. And every time I put on my hat and belt, dress up, and act like an official, I am sure that I am a real official, and no one in the world suspects that I am an actor. I just don't know that the officials who bow and sit, have smiling faces, and act stern and unapproachable, are actually these ancient people who support their families and cry and laugh. So they take a stage, props, scripts, and acting styles, and use them for their entire five internal organs, and don't even realize that they are real actors. How sad!" What this gentleman sees is truly one level above others. He not only tears off the masks of many "officials," allowing us to see the various forms of "officials" in the late Ming Dynasty, but also makes the "officials" of hundreds of years later, who are full of talk about serving the country and the people, unable to laugh or cry. The metaphor is thorough and interesting.

I Curse That Smile of Yours (8) 260

— Wu Yan

This European gentleman then stretched out his sharp, long nose, but in his hazy, drunken eyes, he gradually discerned that this was not beautiful enough. A "No" hummed from his nose, and he raised his head in disappointment. Then he sang in a low, melancholic voice:

"Where is she? My sweet girl..."

The electric light shone on the head of the man wrapped in a black cloth turban, playing on his rough buttocks for three or four minutes, letting this impatient gentleman get a good look. At the same time, taking advantage of his drunken, muddled state, he asked in a slightly teasing tone:

"Is she beautiful?"

No, No, No, No, No, No,

A series of beast-like screams came from his nose. Then he grabbed my shoulders and shook me wildly, laughing roughly, the strong smell of alcohol rushing straight into my nose.

"Ha Ha Ha Chinaman! Ha Ha Ha"

I thought he probably hadn't recognized that this was a man yet, because, for one thing, he couldn't imagine that there would be such a hotel in the world where unfamiliar men and women would sleep in the same bed. His laughter was probably wondering why I would ask such a stupid question.

He played like this for a while, going to every room to play, but finally didn't find a good-looking girl. Of course, this European gentleman was very depressed, and his mouth was still humming that tune he could never finish.

"Where is she? My sweet girl"

But I was extremely happy, extremely joyful, I simply wanted to run to the top of the mountain and shout a few times, so that the mountains, lakes, forests, and marshes would all know my happiness.

But the flames of his greed had not yet been extinguished. In any case, he still wanted to hunt in other places. I also took advantage of the temporary joy and went to have a good time, so I took him to Old Liu's shop.

The horse yard outside the house was soaked in the clear, cold moonlight. The ground was scattered with pale ink-colored shadows of horses, and the sound of teeth grinding straw echoed everywhere. Occasionally, in the slightly distant place, a horse would snort from time to time. The dry fragrance of straw, mixed with the strong smell of horse urine, drifted in waves with the night wind.

The bonfire burning in the open air no longer had a blazing light, but the red embers still remained. The horse groom slept curled up on the side, his raincoat and the moonlight gently covering his body. The dog heard our footsteps and barked madly. The owner, sleeping on the ground, turned over and scolded roughly. I gave him a polite greeting and walked away quietly. The dog still turned around and lay down quietly.

Commercial News, Finance, and Gold Market Fluctuations are Unusually Strong

Silver Price and Exchange Rate Decline, Resulting in a Rise of Three Yuan and Seven Jiao 261

Hong Kong and Shanghai Banking Corporation's Listed Sterling Exchange Rate Remains Unchanged

March Term Standard Gold Drops by Five Jiao

Although the gold market rose yesterday, the situation was not very stable. The market was erratic and fluctuated dramatically. In the early morning, due to the decline in the overseas silver market, both in the UK and the US, the forward silver price on the Five Metals Exchange fell by between 2.9 and 5 tenths of a penny. The exchange rate also fell. The price of raw gold in London rose by one shilling, US cotton fell by 15 points, and US wheat fell by 1.25 points. The gross market was quite stable in the early morning, opening and immediately rising, once approaching the 50 yuan mark, but there were no transactions. Business in Tianjin's Cotton Warehouses Was Quiet Last Year 274

Tianjin Dispatch. In this city's cotton market, buying and selling transactions have always been handled by cotton warehouses. After merchants unload their goods and deliver them to the cotton warehouses for sale, the warehouses deduct a 1% commission and are responsible for providing merchants with working capital and paying drafts. However, astute cotton warehouse managers can observe the situation and seize the opportunity to buy when the market price drops sharply and merchants are eager to sell. This cannot be done without sufficient capital. There are more than 20 cotton warehouses in this city. The business conditions last year were generally unremarkable. The prosperous periods of the cotton market are in the spring, when the rivers thaw and goods from the production areas flow downstream, and in the autumn, when new goods enter the market and demand shows a period of activity. Upon investigation, the sales in the spring of last year were mediocre, and there was no special interest until the summer. Therefore, the futures prices gradually softened, and some cotton warehouses even engaged in short selling without waiting for merchants to sell their goods. Unexpectedly, the spot market revealed a firm trend, and short positions suffered heavy losses during delivery. Some warehouse merchants who had independently engaged in short selling were inevitably affected by losses. By the end of the lunar year, four or five households had their foundations shaken due to the above reasons. The remaining households saw little activity in exports by East and West foreign firms throughout the year, and their profits were also small. However, most were able to cover their expenses with their earnings.

The Tung Oil Market Continues to Close Accounts 281

The tung oil market relies heavily on foreign trade. In recent years, the market has been weak for most of the year due to the decline in foreign sales. Local firms have traditionally focused on domestic sales, but due to the collapse of the rural economy and the decline of all industries, tung oil, which is not a daily necessity, has been more severely affected than other industries. However, each firm has a long history and is primarily focused on stability. Therefore, even if there are profits and losses, they are limited, usually around two or three thousand yuan. The assessment of the value of the inventory will naturally vary. It is not surprising. Most firms have not found it easy to make profits in the past year, so eight or nine out of ten reported a flat result. Even if there are one or two profitable firms, their profits are accumulated over time, which is an exception. All firms will continue to operate as usual this year. The scope of this industry is not large, and the business is stable. Although it cannot be particularly brilliant, it will not suffer major losses. All firms opened for business as usual the day before yesterday.

No. 24 coarse granulated white sugar was sluggish and difficult to sell, falling another 0.05 yuan to 19.80 yuan. The quoted price of Dutch Taikoo red sugar was similar to the previous day, with no transactions. Gao Pianqingchao Gang (High Grade Qingchao brand) offered 50 boxes at a price of 8.70 yuan. The price of white sugar from local factories was affected by the drop in coarse granulated sugar, falling another 0.10 yuan to 18.90 yuan. Ming Qing Bin (Bright Qing Bin) sugar was finally launched yesterday, with an estimated 500 bags offered. The prices were as follows: Tizhuang Qing (Tizhuang Qing) 11.80 yuan, Huanggang Qing (Huanggang Qing) 11.50 yuan to 11.60 yuan, and Ban Nan Qing (Half South Qing) 10.08 yuan to 11.00 yuan to 11.20 yuan. The situation was lackluster.

Silk and Tea: It is Difficult to Expect the Selling Price of Chinese Silk to Rise 283

▲There is No Hope for the Export of Gray Silk. The eight-cocoon gray silk produced in the northeastern provinces is a unique natural product of our country. In recent years, the production of wild silkworm silk in Japan, South Korea, and other countries has increased dramatically, and the sales of artificial silk have encroached upon the market, causing the export of gray silk to plummet. Exports have become exhausted. In the past year (1933), only 1,245 bales were shipped to Europe and the United States. In the year before (1932), 11,475 bales were exported, only about one-tenth of the previous year.

▲It is Difficult to Develop Sales of Foreign Silk Filatures. In the overseas raw silk market, the price of Chinese silk is difficult to rise recently due to the stepped decline and dumping of Japanese silk. Although there were telegrams from New York, Lyon, and other places yesterday morning regarding the trading of yellow and white silk, the prices offered still differed greatly from the cost of Chinese silk, and merchants were unwilling to sell at a loss. Therefore, it is still difficult to develop silk sales. Yesterday, only mainland silk shops purchased 30 bolts of spot white filature silk and 10 bales of Sichuan filature silk. The prices remained firm.

Tea Market: The Tea Market Slightly Opens 284

In the foreign tea market, there have been sporadic negotiations yesterday. The Jardine Matheson purchased 86 boxes of local tea and foreign tea. The opening price of Zhenmei (True Eyebrow) tea was 54 yuan, and the sales price of Xiamei (Shrimp Eyebrow) tea was 48 yuan, with no significant rise or fall compared to the end of the previous period.

Silk and Tea Exports Decline 285

China's foreign trade relies heavily on the transportation and sale of silk and tea to Europe and the United States. However, exports have suddenly declined since the previous year, gradually decreasing. Yesterday, the Pindati (transliterated) of the British company exported only 32 tons of tea, and there was a complete absence of Hu Silk (Huzhou Silk). According to the company, this situation has never happened before, indicating the decline of China's silk and tea. The reason for this is said to be the impact of the low price and dumping of Japanese silk.

Wool Herringbone Fabric is All the Rage for a While 286

Merchants in this street have recently started opening accounts to trade in wool fabrics, which are in demand for spring sales. However, most of them are stamped on credit. Wool herringbone fabrics for overcoats are all the rage and sell particularly well. Clothing stores and Western clothing businesses are purchasing them daily. The demand is especially high in Qipan Street and Daxin Street. Warren herringbone overcoat fabric sells for 7.75 yuan per yard for the actual price. Yongle wool herringbone fabric sells for 6.50 yuan. The Friendship China brand sells for 5.25 yuan. Miye Mai Gao (transliterated) goods sell for 4.10 yuan.

New Angle Iron in the Hardware Market: Sales in Tianjin are Lively 287

Transactions of new angle iron have been developing recently. Although the manufacturers' decorations are ordinary, sales to Tianjin merchants have suddenly become lively. Therefore, the sales volume is much higher than that of British steel plates, new foreign dollars, and other varieties. It is said that the market offered a total of six or seven hundred dan yesterday. The price is estimated at 5.40 yuan per dan, a drop of 0.10 yuan compared to the red market. However, due to the low inventory, the market sentiment is unusually strong. Therefore, for small transactions, the market price still opens at 5.50 yuan, and the credit price for blacksmiths is 6 yuan. It is found that telegrams from overseas are unusually firm. Therefore, there is no downward trend in the market price in this port in the future.

Talking Points

Virtuous Wife and Good Mother 310

— Ms. Jiong

Because of thousands of years of feudal, patriarchal thought tradition, even now, those who claim to be men of the twentieth century, whether old or young, cannot help but hope that women will restore the old duties of virtuous wives and good mothers as their own responsibility, and not allow them to have great development and effort in society! Hoping to be subordinate to men's control and domination day and night. Based on the selfish nature of human beings, we cannot absolutely deny their reasons, but we are more willing to observe in detail and calmly, and recognize the fact that objective conditions have created the past oppression of women and the sole responsibility of only being able to be virtuous wives and good mothers!

Virtuous wife and good mother is a slogan that oppresses us, and it is also the only step for men to stand on their own interests and think about achieving their ultimate goals! Therefore, we must first know that in the current severe period of historical storms, we do not hope to be a purely virtuous wife, nor do we absolutely be a good mother, and eliminate the happiness and meaning of our entire human race; we must also bear a heavy mission and promote the evolution of society forward!

Looking through the history of social evolution, the various processes of the initial development of mankind each have their own production conditions. At that time, there was no distinction between men and women and classes, let alone the difference between oppressors and oppressed.

Due to the demise of the matrilineal system and the rise of the patrilineal system, the original communal system of surnames was broken, and the result of knowing the growth of the system was a major social revolution brought about by the evolution of production methods, and it was the first major revolution in human history. As a result of this revolution, the important position of women in ethnic societies in the past was completely overthrown. From then on, women were completely subordinate to men and in a position of slavery. 丨丨 This should be considered the first time in women's history that they suffered the status of slaves. However, the control of economic power in the hands of men is not an original fact. As Kuno Fu proved, "In the beginning, during the matrilineal system, the economic power of mankind was completely controlled by women. Women were not only the creators of family industry in primitive times, but also the farmers of primitive times. Family industry occupied an important position in the primitive barter era. The initial division of labor was that women planted gardens and vegetables, while men raised livestock; based on this division of labor, all social order was arranged accordingly. Because of the importance of women in the production position, they also occupied an important position in ethnic societies. This important position cannot be overthrown unless there is a fundamental change in production." … We know that women in the past did not have the qualifications to be exclusively virtuous wives and good mothers, but also had great abilities! The overthrow of maternal power was a major failure in the history of women. Since the beginning of the disintegration of tribal systems, production methods have gradually progressed, and when one person's labor can supply the needs of more than one person, this puts women in a subordinate position 丨丨 that is, the so-called slogan that virtuous wife and good mother is the sole responsibility of women, has arisen from this point on. Since men have acquired control over the people's courts, women have become mere reproductive machines and slaves for men's use. That is, as a result of changes and evolution in production methods, when major industries and products are occupied by men, women lose the opportunity for economic independence. Naturally, due to the needs of such life, in the inevitable process, the general women only had to pitifully succumb to the shackles of men! As a result, women are gradually subordinate to men in all aspects of the economy and society, and have completely become appendages and private playthings of men. At this time, the slogan of virtuous wife and good mother was sung high into the clouds, and all the freedom of the women themselves was sacrificed under the control and destruction of the men, and they did not dare to utter a single whimper! What a heartbreaking thing this is!

Originally, the difference between men and women lies only in physiological differences, and there is not much difference at all! Therefore, the labor of men and women should only be appropriate labor based on the physiology of men and women, and there is no huge difference in importance! Therefore, from now on, we should know that in addition to the above-mentioned responsibilities of a virtuous wife and good mother, we should also know that there are many more careers in society waiting for our women's power to develop and pioneer!

To Praise 311

— Ning Yi

Adding a hand or a tree next to the character "奉" (fèng, to offer) will result in characters with different meanings. Adding a hand turns it into "捧" (pěng, to hold/praise), adding a tree turns it into "棒" (bàng, stick/club). "捧" is a verb, "棒" is a noun. The difference between action and inaction is obvious!

"棒" refers to a wooden stick. However, with the addition and usage of external force, it will also move. The Monkey King in the village uses it to make his students quietly recite "Zhao Qian Sun Li?" As for catching thieves in the middle of the night, dragging a stick in hand is enough to make the thief tremble. Clearly, this "棒" has no connection with people. Everyone shakes their head when they hear about being beaten with a stick!

As for the character "捧", it comes from voluntary action. It may be greatly beneficial to praise others, unlike "棒", which is used by others and only knows how to harm others? Therefore, the character "捧" is particularly welcome. In these years, the most important thing to do is to be well-behaved? Since one does not discuss national affairs, one naturally talks nonsense. Since the "棒" is not welcomed, one has to be agreeable and talk about the universally admired character "捧"?

As mentioned earlier, praising comes from voluntary action, but this cannot be generalized. Facts often contradict this. For example, actors often host banquets before going on stage, inviting people who will say good or bad things about their magic? As for the invited people, their mouths have already been stuffed with things! Therefore, according to the theorem "If you take someone's money, you have to help them avoid disaster", they try their best to praise them in the newspapers, even if the art is really terrible. The above belongs to the passive category.

Those who act voluntarily are actually selfish? The driving force is nothing more than benefiting oneself or harming others! When you see a wealthy and powerful person, you might as well flatter them to their face and write an article praising them in the newspaper; or sing their praises. As for those with malicious intent, for example, when a beautiful Kun Opera actor goes on stage, people often cheer and applaud wildly. In fact, they are not admiring the beauty of the art, but want to use this to advance themselves, to get the actor's favor, and to corrupt their mind? All of this belongs to the category of voluntary action.

There are also those who do not want to praise others but need to be praised by others. Officials need people to beat the drums beside them? Only then can fortune come to them. Furthermore, while in office, there must always be people singing their praises in the newspapers, which is of great benefit? As for a certain position that has been determined, and when people are being scouted, that is precisely an insinuation that whoever is praised the most will get the job. Therefore, if you don't want to do it, that's fine, but if you want to do it, you need praisers. In the past, Yuan Shikai dreamed of becoming emperor, and what about ascending the throne and setting a reign title? If no one praised him, he really couldn't bring himself to do it. As for the puppet in the Northeast that we neither recognize nor have wiped out, it is naturally also the work of praising. With Zheng's reverse persuasion, and even those short enemies who do not turn to good thoughts agreeing, naturally their skin has thickened! In short, with "praising", things will naturally become chaotic.

I, You, He 312

— Xiren

When I came downstairs to answer the phone, my friend smilingly handed me the receiver. This was originally an ordinary matter. I receive countless phone calls every day, and I've never seen him with such a comical expression. So, I couldn't help but ask, "Who is it?" My friend didn't answer; he made another funny face and ran away. Miss, this is what surprised me. The voice on the other end of the line was a woman's. No wonder my friend acted that way. People say I know too little about women, and I really can't get close to them. I don't know how to be humble to women; I don't know how to be gentle in my speech with women... In short, I know too little about women. Yet, I received a phone call from a woman, Miss. If this were six months ago, after hearing the voice, I could have unhesitatingly asked, "Are you ××?" But now I can't. After trying in vain for a long time, it turned out to be you, Miss.

Time flies so fast. It's another New Year, and we've all grown another year older. What do you ask me to do during the New Year? Miss, what can I tell you? If it weren't for bills and demands for payment flying in, I wouldn't even know another year had begun. So, I simply replied, "Nothing!" At this moment, the voice on the phone changed to a man's voice. His manner of speaking was indeed very gentle. After addressing me as Mr. ×, he offered New Year's greetings. Please forgive my rudeness at the time; I didn't say a word of courtesy. Speaking of which, Miss, I didn't come to congratulate you when you got married and ask for a cup of wedding wine. I still don't know how to deal with an unfamiliar man. Saying I know too little about women is only half the story; I know too little about social interactions between people, or rather, the means of what amounts to deception.

Miss, thank you both for thinking of an old friend after returning from your travels in the South. You specially invited me to dinner at the start of the New Year. In principle, I shouldn't decline under any circumstances, but in the past six months, I haven't made any progress. I'm still that kind of man who knows nothing. I feel ashamed to face an old friend, ashamed to face the old friend's companion whom I haven't met! I lied to you, saying that my workplace has a banquet. Of course, the old friend knows me. I clearly heard you say, "He's lying." At the same time, two laughs came through, probably because you were leaning on his shoulder, and your 'he' said many polite things. Ah! I know too little about using deception. You saw through my lie at the first shot, so I didn't even say "Thank you" or "Goodbye" to him because I'm still someone who knows too little about the ways of social interaction. Goodbye then, and Happy New Year!

Who Defends the Shanghai School? 313

— A'tan

I wrote an article in the Shanghai local supplement of the Shen Bao, "On Selling Writing for a Living," which elicited an article from Mr. Qingnong. He said: A'tan misunderstood Mr. Shen Congwen's original intention and defended the "Shanghai School," "aiding the wicked." In fact, it wasn't that A'tan misunderstood Mr. Shen Congwen's article; it was that Mr. Qingnong misunderstood A'tan's article. First of all, A'tan doesn't look up to people of the Shanghai School. Therefore, when he saw Mr. Cao Juren's words, "Both the Shanghai School and the Beijing School should be swept away," he felt it was absolutely right. And he agrees with his statement that "Between the two, it is better to be Beijing than Shanghai." Because the Shanghai School has some connection with society, while the Beijing School wants to break away from society (please refer to Mr. Cao's original article). So, it's clear that A'tan doesn't consider "making money" to be a characteristic of the Shanghai School (therefore, he said "the so-called commercial competition includes many things"). A'tan wrote that article "On Selling Writing for a Living" simply because of the association with the four words "commercial competition." (I remember stating that in the original article.) A'tan's article was neither a response to Mr. Shen Congwen nor a defense of the Shanghai School. Therefore, even the "he" mentioned in the "somewhat harsh" statement doesn't refer to Mr. Shen Congwen, but to those who attack others by selling words for money without principles. I don't understand what Mr. Qingnong misunderstood.

Mr. Qingnong repeatedly tells us who the Shanghai School is and what types of Shanghai School there are, for which we can be grateful. Because we can "recognize traitors and attack them." Even A'tan believes that people who are "merchants and thieves" should be attacked. They even sell their personalities. In A'tan's original article, it is repeatedly mentioned whether what is being sold is poison or aphrodisiac, which is extremely clear.

To put it more clearly, the idea of A'tan's article is simply to explain that selling writing is not shameful. The "Beijing School" mocks the "Shanghai School" for having a "commercial competition," but selling writing isn't entirely "Shanghai School," and simply selling writing doesn't constitute "Shanghai School." A'tan used Dostoevsky as an example, but is Dostoevsky a Shanghai School writer?

Mr. Shen Congwen's "commercial competition" is like saying that thieves eat. A'tan's article simply explains that not everyone who eats is a thief; the question is whether they "steal or not." That's all.

Regarding the "merchants and thieves" types, Mr. Qingnong says that those of us who "sell writing for a living" can "only recognize them as "traitors" and attack them." If A'tan were a little more arrogant, he would say that he and those who "sell aphrodisiacs and arsenic," as specially mentioned in A'tan's original article, are no different from those who sell cod liver oil. As for Mr. Qingnong, who hopes that "Shanghai School writers" will create brilliant glory in the literary world, please forgive my further arrogance: "Mr. Qingnong's forgiveness of the 'Shanghai School' is much greater than A'tan's."

There's no question that Shanghai School writers are worthy of attack. Even A'tan advocates sweeping them away, but if the only crime of Shanghai School writers is making money (naturally, not selling their personalities), is that something that lies in A'tan's heart? Naturally, Mr. Shen Congwen and even Mr. Qingnong don't single out making money as the crime of Shanghai School writers, so A'tan's article isn't defending the Shanghai School, of course.

The Beautiful Nanny 314

— Aixi

The necessary condition for being a nanny, in theory, is that she can work and be clean. Whether or not she is beautiful doesn't seem to matter. But although that's what people say, the reality is that it doesn't play out that way!

Especially in a glamorous city like Shanghai!

A few months ago, a new neighbor moved into the back building: an old man and a young woman. A few days later, I learned that they were a father-in-law and daughter-in-law, and they got along quite well. Her mother-in-law was a "amah" who had studied abroad, and the son's noble occupation was unknown.

In recent days, the relationship between the father-in-law and daughter-in-law seems to be developing cracks day by day. They are often heard arguing loudly and softly, and they each cook their own meals, quite like "living in the same house but eating separately." Suddenly, the daughter-in-law began to apply rouge and powder every morning, using all sorts of artificial embellishments. Moreover, she couldn't sit still in the house, so she left early and returned late every day—but I don't know what she was doing.

"Sister-in-law of the back building, where are you going?" One day, when she was dressed up and preparing to go out, I asked with a smile. "Going to look for business, to help people."

"No wonder I've seen you at home these past few days; you're looking for business!"

"Yes! What's the point of a young person being idle at home?"

"Did you find anything?"

"I had a business the day before yesterday, but because the master wanted to take me with them when they went out, I wasn't happy."

"So you have to find something else?"

"No, yesterday someone introduced me to the mansion at ×× Lane ×× Number: the wife of this family just died, and they want someone to take care of the children; there's even extra money every day!" She said rather proudly.

"Sleeping over?"

"Not coming back. Sleeping in the same room as the young master, but on two beds. I sleep with the children. The young master said: the nanny has to be beautiful and clean. I'm going to see his house today—I guess it should be suitable!"

She walked away smiling and speaking, full of the joys of spring.

It wasn't even two hours later. She came back to move her bedding. Outside stood a man holding a child, naturally indicating that the business had been successful. However, just as she was taking the bedding out the door, she turned her head and glared at the back building, cursing fiercely, "You old geezer..."

"Let's go! Amah!" She suddenly heard the man holding the child outside calling out, and she immediately, in the laughter of "Coming! Coming! Young master!" twisted her body, putting on a "smile that launches a thousand charms"!

"Nannies need to be beautiful too; so that's how it is!" That thought was deeply imprinted in my mind.

A Mao's New Clothes 315

— Yier

It really was a great stroke of luck. A Mao, who usually wore patched and ragged shirts and trousers, actually got a new set of clothes made at the end of the year, ready to compete for some face in the New Year.

She had gone several years without new clothes for the New Year. Like the year before last, although her mother had firmly promised to make her a set, it ultimately didn't happen because her father, one day while pushing a wheelbarrow on the road, was knocked over by a motorcycle cart and was fined a dollar by the police, which affected the planned new clothes.

After this New Year, she would be just nine years old. Children don't really understand how to be fashionable, but she always felt that not having new clothes to wear for the New Year was a shameful fact.

I remember that the year before last, because she was still wearing that worn-out outfit on New Year's Day, she was ridiculed by many girls she played with, which made her very frustrated. So, from that time on, she made a grand wish that, no matter what, she would always try her best to negotiate with her parents to make her a new set of clothes to avenge her long-held resentment.

Sure enough, this time the goal was achieved. A set of new clothes made of green-striped foreign cloth, bought for nine dimes and two cents, was finally made by her mother, who secretly worked four nights under the lamp. Although her mother's needlework wasn't necessarily that good, the finished product fit quite well. When A Mao was asked to try it on, her father praised it for being very fitting, and she jumped up and down, as happy as could be.

So, she said to her father and mother:

"I'm so happy, I have new clothes to wear for the New Year!"

The father smiled; the mother replied:

"A Mao! Good, no need to have a long face on the first day of the New Year! But you have to cherish them and not get them dirty! After the Lantern Festival, you must change them. Wear them again on festival days or when watching lively events!"

Because of these new clothes, A Mao looked forward to the New Year coming sooner every day. It was only with great difficulty that she got to the end of the year. That night, she and her parents had their New Year's Eve dinner. Her father gave her twelve copper coins as New Year's money and instructed her:

"A Mao, go to sleep quickly at night, so you can get up early tomorrow to go out and play."

"Dad, okay, get up early tomorrow to go out and play!" She imitated her father's words, and then turned her head: "Mom, wake me up at five o'clock tomorrow morning, I want to get up and wear my new clothes to wish Dad and Mom a happy New Year."

On the morning of the first day of the New Year, a burst of firecrackers rang out, and A Mao woke up on her own without her mother calling her. At the moment she just opened her eyes, she lay alone in the quilt, savoring the dream she had that night.

She dreamed of wearing that newly made green-striped foreign cloth short shirt and trousers, and going to play with many familiar children in an open space. She also brought some snacks and ate them very happily. Moreover, all the playmates praised her new clothes, saying they were very beautiful. She felt that this was the most glorious day of her life, and therefore became proud.

Thinking of this, she couldn't help but smile, and then shook her mother, who was sleeping beside her, shouting that she wanted to get her new clothes to wear. At this time, her mother was awakened by her. She coughed, then turned over and stroked her daughter's fine hair with her hand, coaxing her lovingly:

"A Mao, are you awake? It's still early. I'll tell you, last night when Dad went to sleep, he told me to tell A Mao when she woke up tomorrow that she didn't need to wear her new clothes. There's no great point in wearing new clothes for the New Year. We plan to go to your uncle's house for the Lantern Festival, and it will be good to wear them then, so it's a little more fresh. When your uncle sees them, he will be even happier!"

"No, no! I want to wear them today!" Her eyes widened, and she shouted anxiously.

"Good A Mao, be good and listen to Mom! The black cloth shirt you wore for the Mid-Autumn Festival is also ready. I washed it clean for you the day before yesterday."

"Who wants to wear that one? That one has patches on the front and sleeves! I don't want it, I must wear my new clothes! If I don't have new clothes to wear for the New Year, people will bully me!" A Mao was almost crying, saying it with her upper and lower lips tightly closed.

The father also woke up, and also comforted her gently: "Good child, listen to Mom, or it will be good to wear them on the ninth day, the ninth day is the Jade Emperor's birthday."

"No, wear them today, wear them on the ninth day too, and wear them to my uncle's house too!" A Mao said stubbornly.

After several attempts to coax her, she still wouldn't give in. In great distress, the father finally became angry and slapped her twice in the face. The reaction, of course, was A Mao's crying. In the end, thanks to the mother's many kind words to persuade her, and giving her some pocket money, she was tricked into staying put.

After breakfast, A Mao had no choice but to put on that old black cloth shirt and slipped outside to play. The couple stayed at home, sitting there in between them. The mother suddenly sighed and said:

"Poor people are just destined to have no luck. They can't even let her wear a set of new clothes that have been made out to meet people properly. It's enough to coax her, what does a child know, why did you hit her!"

"Where did I really want to hit her? But I felt too sad, so I couldn't help but get angry; sigh!"

"The rice shop owner wouldn't budge, I told you to just take this quilt, but you insisted on those new clothes." The mother said with red eyes.

"The quilt! It's so cold, without this quilt, I'm afraid we'll freeze to death... And the Chen family next door owes two oceans, I begged bitterly, and they finally agreed to postpone it to the middle of the month." The father said with infinite sadness.

While the couple were coughing and sighing, A Mao suddenly came crying in from outside the door, intermittently sobbing: "Mom! Give me my new clothes to wear! People are bullying me again. They said I look like a beggar. Those new clothes weren't bought with Dad's money, they were bought with the four two-dime bills Mom picked up in a garbage dump in an alley the day before yesterday, why won't you let me wear them!"

Their hearts felt like they were being stabbed with needles. They couldn't find a word to comfort her. They could only see tears streaming down their faces like a spring of water!

Husband and Wife (5) 317

"Fifth Master Zhou, don't pay; just take it." Xu San stood up from the dirt floor.

"Take it. Good stuff." Zhou Chunrong gave him the money and lay down on the bed, taking Mr. Cao's cigarette.

After receiving the money, Xu San couldn't find the lantern he wanted in the corner of the room, so he shrunk his head and went out. A cold air rushed onto his face again. In the pitch-black sky, the faint wind was blowing, and a surge of heat moved in his heart. A group of peddlers passed him, carrying burdens, their feet in straw sandals stepping heavily in the bone-chilling mud, making a "chatter, chatter" sound. Gently, gently, he pushed open the door of his house. It was dark inside. He familiarly walked inside.

Before he reached his own room, a woman's voice came from the room, asking,

"Who is it?" The question was issued after a laugh.

"Me." The answer was dry, familiar.

"What do you want?" The question was immediately passed out, as if asking a stranger.

"Getting cigarettes." Xu San understood that there was a guest smoking in the room, so he slowed down his pace.

"I'll bring them to you."

So Xu San stopped. The drawer in the room rang slightly, and then he heard the question: "How much money is it?" After getting the answer, after a while, his wife, Third Sister, came out of the room with a lamp, and the dark outer room suddenly became bright.

The lamplight shone on about half of her thirty-year-old face, which had the enchanting beauty of a woman who was getting old, but she glanced at her husband with extreme coldness. The side silhouette was reflected on the wall, the back of the silhouette on the wall was her hair, and the silhouette swayed slightly. "Who is it?" Xu San asked his wife in a low voice, taking the cigarette pack.

The silhouette's lips also moved, in an extremely low voice. "Wang Chaofeng of Hu Yitai's."

The husband turned and walked away. She called out "Don't forget to flick the ash," and after the husband hummed and walked out, she closed the door tightly, inspected outside the room, and then returned to the room.

She put the lamp on the table, turned down the flame a little, poured tea for Mr. Wang, placed the teacup steadily on the smoking tray, and sat in front of Wang Chaofeng's angled knees. The man propped up his slightly leaning body with his left hand, and his right hand reached up from behind her, under her clothes. Third Sister leaned on him in the situation. A playful laughter started in the yellow light.

She stood up and lay down again in her original position on the opposite side. Both pairs of eyes were looking at the flame inside the round-mouthed glass cover, as if the dim interest of this small flame was more interesting than the movies in the city.

The man smoked, speaking at the same time; all the movements were unhurried, and the black, small particles that were swelling up on the smoke skewer were turning on his left index finger very deftly and skillfully. She glanced at the man and said,

Film Special

George Raft's Fear of Women (Part 2) 318

— Mizhai

"There are really too many of these kinds of women in Hollywood. When they can't get in through the front door, they try to stick to a star, preparing to file an abandonment lawsuit in the future, which can at least give them publicity, as a shortcut to entering the film industry. Sometimes, this plan actually succeeds, so the rest all follow suit, leading to the current situation, where no man in Hollywood can be said to have security.

"There are really too many kinds of women's tricks. The most common is the mother-daughter combo. For example, you live in an apartment, and suddenly one day, a new neighbor moves in next door: a very amiable middle-aged woman, with a girl. That girl, seeing you, will definitely say, "Oh, this is great, to be able to live in the same house as a big star." Her innocent look will make you not suspect her of having any ambitions. You might invite them over for tea, or take them to visit the studio, or even introduce the girl to the company. If she can make it, that would be great. But if she doesn't succeed, then her mother will speak up. You quickly think of a way for her; otherwise, she will slander you, accusing you of some crime. At that time, the most common method is to take out your checkbook and write a check. There are too many of these kinds of mothers in Hollywood. She's in the back, arranging and directing everything, making it impossible for you to defend against or escape.

"Everyone thinks that the phone numbers of big stars are absolutely secret, but clever women will always find a way to find them out. Or one day, you receive a phone call, the other person is a woman, she says she was introduced by so-and-so. At that time, you have no way to verify it, you can only vaguely agree to her request and meet her. She comes, and you may find that what so-and-so said was a fabrication, but she claims to be a fan who admires you, so you don't want to offend her. Or you think she's very clever, very interesting... They are almost all clever and interesting young women... Then you feel it's okay to deal with her. Slowly, she gradually reveals her intentions, wanting to demand fur coats, jewelry, and other things from you. If you don't agree, she will turn against you and bite you; if you agree to her, then there's no way to fill her insatiable desires, so you're in a dilemma. "Once, it was extremely dangerous. I was shooting a scene in the studio, and a woman was standing next to me, holding a notebook and pencil in her arms. She said she wanted to talk to me. I thought she was a reporter, so I agreed. When the scene was finished, I told her to wait ten minutes, preparing to go and remove my makeup. Unexpectedly, as soon as I entered the dressing room, she followed me in. She said she was used to seeing people in the theater and film industry, so it didn't matter to see me changing clothes. Believing her words, I took off my costume in front of her. Unexpectedly, taking me by surprise, she also took off all her clothes. I don't know what her good intentions were, but it took a lot of effort to persuade her to leave. From then on, my dressing room was locked whenever I went in or out. Do you think I'm afraid of women or not? "After talking for so long, what's the solution? The answer is very difficult, the reason is that ordinary people are too easily deceived by propaganda and doubt the character of movie stars. The saying "Where there's smoke, there's fire" doesn't apply here. Many breach of promise lawsuits in Hollywood are completely groundless. Of course, justice can be obtained in court, but people in society don't wait for the court's judgment, but are lightly influenced by propaganda. Therefore, general movie stars don't dare to give up their careers and prospects to go to court, because even if they win the lawsuit in the future, their reputation has been stained, and their future may be dimmed because of it. After calculating, it's best to swallow their anger, spend some money unjustly, and settle it privately. But the crime of extortion and intimidation grows because of this, and general male stars regard associating with women as a fearful path." (End)

Film Commentary

Review of "The Road to Light" 319

— Sha Si

In today's society, two typical lifestyles are prevalent: one is wealthy, with no worries about clothing, food, or housing, and a happy family; the other is impoverished, suffering from hunger and cold, with no place to settle, and a family that not only lacks happiness but may even be torn apart. An artistic work that can capture such typical realities and portray them will undoubtedly leave a deep impression. The author of "The Road to Light" used the realistic event of Chen Tai's economic oppression, which led to the death of his wife and the scattering of his children, as the subject matter. This effort is commendable. However, after grasping such a real subject, the author did not treat it in a consistently realistic manner, losing the serious and conscientious attitude that such a subject deserved. The author considered trivial interests and added unnecessary and unrealistic interludes, such as having Chen Tai sell medicine as a gimmick. This not only lacks sufficient realism but also gives the entire play a sense of "inappropriateness" in its development and presentation, given the central theme. However, the author's juxtaposition of the singing and feasting in the wealthy family's home with Chen Tai's home has considerable power in expressing the film's theme, although it is a bit overdone.

There are also some very coincidental interludes. These accidental events also weaken the development, expression, power, and tension of the entire play. For example, Chen Tai's accidental finding of a newspaper in the park to look for a job does not seem to forcefully express his fear of unemployment. Of course, I am not saying that Chen Tai should not read the newspaper to look for a job; on the contrary, Chen Tai should intentionally look for newspapers, wouldn't that be more tense and powerful than the accidental finding of a newspaper?

In addition, Chen Tai and the unemployed workers competing to confess at the Public Security Bureau (?), and going to the Northwest to reclaim land, all lack sufficient realism. This does not inject much power into the overall development and presentation of the film; especially the ending of going to the Northwest to reclaim land seems even more forced. Furthermore, turning unemployed workers into thieves cannot be considered a moving stroke; it is not to say that unemployed workers in today's society never resort to theft, but this situation is ultimately not common. Grasping special, i.e., atypical, events or characters to express them is very problematic in terms of effect.

In short, because the author did not deal with the adopted subject head-on and realistically express the theme, this film cannot be a very powerful, successful, and complete work.

However, the director's directing techniques and the actors' performances are quite successful, which gives the film considerable power. In particular, Zheng Junli's and Tan Ying's (Tan Ying's makeup is too young) performances, using a slow tempo to portray their characters, are the most suitable and powerful techniques. However, when Zheng Junli unexpectedly returns, Tan Ying should not slam the door shut twice; she should hesitate and slowly close the door to coordinate with Zheng Junli's tempo. This would avoid showing disharmony. There are many examples of this. This shows the director's considerable responsibility. Also, Zheng Junli's makeup seems like stage makeup. Makeup on the silver screen cannot be so rough; it needs to be much more refined than stage makeup so that it does not show on the screen.

However, the point must be reiterated. Although this film distorts reality to the greatest extent in the end, the author's original intention would never have been so. Moreover, we have proven in various ways that the original author made Chen Tai realize that the anti-imperialist war was their proper "way out," but due to certain circumstances, he proposed the slogan of going to the Northwest.

Review of "The Queen of the Cattle Ranch" 320

— Li Qiong

The Thundering Herd

丨Carlton丨

American Western films are flooding the Chinese film market like a tide, which makes Chinese audiences very familiar with them. I think they must have a deep understanding of Western films themselves. At the same time, in the field of film criticism, the social basis of Western films has been pointed out countless times.

However, among a series of similar films, "The Queen of the Cattle Ranch" is the most blatant. It clearly and boldly depicts the cruelty and barbarity of white people invading the indigenous people. The white people plunder the indigenous people's cattle hides in droves, and when they encounter the resistance of the indigenous people, they use the latest weapons to slaughter them miserably. After watching it, can't we prove the author's intention here? Isn't it enough to explain the political significance of so-called martial arts films?

Of course, any kind of American film will not lack the interweaving of women and love. Here, if we are not careful, we will inevitably only see the heroic and mighty image of heroes robbing women. However, no matter how many times the indigenous people are plundered, and no matter how many times there are major conflicts in the end, we will not overlook this important theme, right?

In terms of performance, perhaps we will be overwhelmed by the constant riding and shooting, and the constant tense scenes. Naturally, this is not just a matter of good or bad technique. If we are willing to not ignore the close unity of content and form, and if we absolutely believe that form is the expression of content, then the success of this technique fully illustrates the greatest harm of the content.

Perhaps some people say that Chinese audiences are not necessarily harmed by it, and can only watch the magic of riding and shooting, because we have no indigenous people to invade. However, won't the concept of invasion exist in their hearts? Readers, please think about it again and again.

Review of "Kongo" (African Kongo) 321

— Liu Shi

Kongo 丨 Screening in Shanghai 丨

After watching this film, I felt a deep chill. After watching it, this is a true portrayal of the character of civilized people. Slaughter, cruel atrocities. Is this the nature of mankind? Only so-called civilized people would do this.

Here, the author fully describes the deceit, selfishness, hypocrisy, and cruelty of civilized people. Although he cleverly explains that the protagonist took extremely cruel revenge measures because he had been bullied by people. He seduces the enemy's daughter, he detains the doctor. Perhaps the author regrets the protagonist's personality disorder. However, he is ultimately cruel, and his nature is selfish. When he discovers that the enemy's daughter is his own flesh and blood, he finally releases her. Here, of course, there is another effect, which is the American film author's consistent emphasis on love. Because she already has a lover, and her lover is so infatuated with her, this cruel civilized man grants her happiness without any hesitation. Naturally, this woman is fortunately his own daughter. If she were ultimately the enemy's daughter, would he also preserve her life for the sake of her love?

Apart from this, let's look again. Wasn't the protagonist very cleverly conquering that group of savages in Africa? And wasn't that group of indigenous people completely subdued by authority? Okay, this explains that the white civilized people are the masters of the world, and the indigenous people are always slaves like cattle and horses. Thus, the conquered submit to their masters, and civilization is the god of the world. However, what is even more despicable is the exaggeration of so-called virtue. This masking of the truth of barbaric behavior has become the most self-satisfied aspect of civilized people. However, in the end, the protagonist frankly says: "This is where my authority lies, my command is law." Isn't this an exposure of the truth?

Perhaps some people think that this is not a true record, perhaps they think that there is no such country in reality, but aren't the cruel imperialists the rulers of five-sixths of the world? Especially we Chinese people are not subdued by the violence of the powerful, and even feel suffocated when breathing? And haven't we already heard the cries of resistance from slaves all over the world?丨 This is a microcosm.

Besides, what else do I want to say? The director cleverly showed the majesty of the brutal person, and the protagonist, Houston, also fully expressed that terrible character, making us tremble. After watching this film, can we still laugh? In my mind, I often retain the terrifying image of those demons.

Film Novel

Queen Christina (10) (2) 322

— Hu Chen

Oxenstierna reminded him from the side: "Doesn't Your Excellency have a handwritten letter from your country's king?" Antonio still couldn't speak, only gestured to his attendants with his hand. The attendant then presented a large envelope, tied with ribbon on the outside, and sealed with a large wax seal, to Prime Minister Oxenstierna, who then presented it to the Queen. Antonio then opened his mouth and said: "Your Majesty, I am a special envoy sent by my country's king. I have important matters related to both countries to report to Your Majesty, and I hope Your Majesty will listen." The Queen handed the large envelope to Oxenstierna and said to the Spanish ambassador: "We will meet again in the inner court soon, and we will talk about it then. For now, please rest assured that our country has great respect for your monarch and the special envoy of your monarch, and we will treat you with as much courtesy as possible." The formal audience thus came to an end. Antonio bowed and thanked, and also withdrew. Christina stood still and watched him leave. The cunning Magnus understood everything after seeing that scene. But Christina still didn't feel anything.

Christina waited quietly for Antonio to come to the inner private chamber for a meeting. Attendants ran in one by one, arranging many foods such as wine and fruit. In the outer chamber, there was also a band playing delicate music. Ebba walked in. She told Christina that the Minister of Finance was requesting an audience. Christina refused to see him, but Ebba tried to persuade her. However, Christina was very firm, and Ebba could only report back to Magnus with fear and trepidation. Magnus was inevitably resentful in his heart because Christina refused to see him. He lingered there, waiting for the Spanish ambassador to arrive. Once the Spanish ambassador arrived, he stepped forward and pretended to greet him very politely. He intentionally or unintentionally talked about the weather in Sweden. He said: "Our country's weather is only bearable for those who are used to it, and is very unsuitable for foreigners, so I advise Your Excellency to be careful and protect yourself." Antonio said: "Are Your Excellency's words a threat?" Magnus said with a sneer: "This is advice." His voice was like a cold wind, piercing straight into Antonio's heart. However, Ebba had already run out from the inner chamber to invite him in, so he didn't say anything, bowed to Magnus, and followed Ebba in.

What made Christina feel very disappointed was that Antonio's meeting in the private chamber was still restrained and extremely formal. Every time Christina wanted to get close to him, to return to the previous situation, he would block her with extremely short language. He said to Christina: "My country's king has long heard of Your Majesty's virtue, and has specially sent me here to pay my respects, to communicate our feelings, and to wish to form a marital alliance with Your Majesty." This shocked Christina, because although Prime Minister Oxenstierna had told her about it, she always thought that this time the Spanish King sent a special envoy here was probably to revise the treaty, or about matters of art, and never expected that he was coming to propose marriage to her. She asked Antonio: "Is this your mission?" Antonio said: "My country's king, with the utmost sincerity and respect, has ordered me to come here to propose marriage, and I must ask Your Majesty to consider and accept." Christina let out a very miserable sound and said: "Why do you treat me so harshly?" Antonio said: "I am in the position of an envoy, and I am here on the orders of my monarch. I dare not be harsh, nor dare I harbor any private opinions." Christina said: "Are we going to pretend from now on that there is no relationship between us?" (To be continued)
